Will Russia and Japan Really Go to War? The Japanese Have Already Seized the Management Rights of the Chinese Eastern Railway, Russian Troops Concentrated on the Border According to London

(London) The increasingly deteriorating relations between Russia and Japan have aroused anxiety among the general public. The Moscow authorities are very angry because (Manchukuo) has arbitrarily appointed a director of the Chinese Eastern Railway Bureau, taking precedence over Russian director Rudy, and interfering with the Russian railway management rights. At the same time, negotiations on the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway have completely stalled, and both sides are trying to block each other's trade on the railway. Soviet Russia has now issued an important order to provide preferential treatment to farmers in the Amur and Primorsky provinces and increase the monthly salaries of the Far East Army, and it is openly stated that this is for the purpose of strengthening defense. London believes that Russia has 250,000 troops stationed on the Amur border, as well as 450 aircraft in Vladivostok and Shuangchengpu, including 40 heavy bombers. It is said that Russia's conclusion of a non-aggression treaty with Poland and its efforts to seek friendship with France are enough to allow it to act freely in the Far East. (Reuters, 16th)

Takahashi Advocates Implementing Retaliatory Tariffs to Cope with the World's Markets

(Tokyo) The trade wars and tariff wars between countries around the world are becoming increasingly fierce. In order to cope with this commercial war, the Japanese government is studying the theory of retaliatory tariffs by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Ministry of Commerce and Industry is considering trade management proposals, and the Ministry of Finance, which is in charge of tariff control, also recognizes its necessity. Finance Minister Takahashi expressed his views on the 15th, strongly advocating the necessity of establishing countermeasures such as retaliatory tariffs and trade management. That is, Finance Minister Tan said, "Today, the trade relations between countries are dangerous. Japan should resist with appropriate weapons. The retaliatory tariff plan is a necessary weapon for this. The enactment of laws to manage exchange rates was thought at the time that the laws could manage trade, but in fact this is not the case. Tariff wars can be dealt with by retaliatory tariff wars, but under various circumstances, tariffs alone are not a sufficient method. It is also possible to implement import bans when necessary. The future of trade is unpredictable. In order to deal with future situations, the government intends to submit a bill to the parliament to obtain the authority to deal with various opportunities." (Japanese United News, 16th) (Tokyo) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has decided on a policy. After the Japanese-Indian negotiations are completed to resolve the problem of the oppression of Japanese goods around the world, it has ordered a special committee of the Trade Deliberation Council to make preparations. The means are to set up commercial officers in Batavia to serve as an intermediary organization for trade between the Union of South Africa and Japan. At the same time, exchange ministers or representatives from both sides to resolve various issues, and exchange envoys with India and Australia to maintain Japanese commercial rights. (Japanese United News, 16th)

Germany Also Advocates Rejecting Japanese Goods

(Tokyo) According to a telegram from Japanese Ambassador to Germany Nagai to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the impact of Japanese goods, which are like a flood everywhere in the world, is not direct in Germany, but recently there has been a kind of discussion, which even uses the words "yellow peril." The reason for the entry and exit of Japanese goods is that the European countries are all engrossed in political struggles. If common defense measures are not taken decisively at this time, it is feared that the time of the complete annihilation of Europe will arrive. Therefore, those who are engaged in Japanese goods in Germany have been discussing countermeasures and all believe that the Japanese government should take the following measures: (1) Conclude agreements with various countries individually. (2) For countries with no treaties or discriminatory treatment, seek appropriate means in terms of tariffs. (3) When establishing export associations, formulate regulations that are stronger than compulsory enterprise alliances. (4) The government and the people should jointly establish appropriate systems. (5) Stop imitating trademarks. (6) While Japan's economy is developing, it is also in the interest of raw material countries. The advanced countries should be explained its meaning in opening up new markets. (Dentsu News Agency, 16th)

Taking Over Shanhaiguan Actively Underway; Both Sides to Continue Negotiations on Details; Complete Takeover Expected by Year-End

The issue of reopening the Beining Railway urgently needs resolution. According to communications from Beiping, regarding the matter of taking over Shanhaiguan, personnel were previously sent to Shanhaiguan to negotiate the takeover procedures with Japanese representatives. However, due to the Japanese side creating additional obstacles, the takeover could not be completed as scheduled. Recent back-and-forth consultations have resulted in some progress. After the Shanhaiguan meeting, Igi, the head of the Japanese Special Service Agency in Shanhaiguan, once came to Beiping to meet with He and Huang to discuss the matter. At that time, it was agreed that Igi would be responsible for specifying the date of return and the takeover procedures and notifying the Chinese side to implement the takeover. Igi then exchanged telegrams with the Kwantung Army. At the same time, Tao Shangming, the representative responsible for the Chinese side, was consulting with Huang Fu and Yu Xuezhong in both Beiping and Tianjin, seeking instructions and exchanging views with Shibayama, the military attaché of the Japanese Embassy, and Umezu, the commander of the Japanese North China Garrison Army. The day before yesterday, Tao met with Umezu in Tianjin and agreed to telegraph Igi, inviting him to Tianjin for another meeting to discuss the details of the takeover. Tao came to Beiping this afternoon (14th) to meet with He and Huang, seeking instructions, and at 3 p.m., accompanied by Yuan Tai, the newly appointed magistrate of Linyu County, visited Shibayama at the Japanese Embassy to discuss everything. Shibayama telegraphed Igi, asking him to come to Tianjin immediately to meet with Tao and others. Tao plans to go to Tianjin tomorrow evening (15th) with Yuan Tai to wait for Igi. If Igi can arrive in Tianjin in the next few days, the takeover details will be discussed in Tianjin. The representatives of both sides are Tao Shangming, Yuan Tai, Umezu, and Igi. If necessary, Yu Xuezhong and Shibayama will also participate. In case Igi does not have time to come to Tianjin, Yuan Tai will first have a diplomatic meeting with Umezu in Tianjin and then rush to Haiyangzhen before the 20th to take over his post, so as not to miss the deadline set by the provincial government. Tao Shangming will then go to Shanhaiguan to negotiate the detailed takeover procedures with Igi, with the aim of completing the takeover by the end of the year. Regarding the East Luocheng walled city, where negotiations have been obstructed, both sides are avoiding formal negotiations. Currently, the Japanese barracks in that area are mostly completed, and the market has also been planned. In fact, there is no hope of returning it. The opinions of both sides on the other minor issues are generally close and do not pose a major problem. The Chinese negotiators hope that Igi will arrive in Tianjin immediately to fully agree on all procedures, so that the Linyu County government can move to Yucheng, allowing the newly appointed County Magistrate Yuan Tai to go directly to Shanhaiguan to take office. Yuan graduated from the Zhejiang Military Academy in the late Qing Dynasty and studied in Japan. He has a classmate relationship with Huang Fu, is very experienced, and is also capable. It may be more appropriate to have him deal with this difficult situation.

The issue of reopening the Beining Railway, which is related to the takeover of Shanhaiguan, also urgently needs to be resolved. During the previous visit to Beiping by Okamura, Deputy Chief of Staff of the Kwantung Army, to negotiate the resolution of various issues in the war zone, the issues of taking over the various passes of the Great Wall and reopening the railway were discussed at the same time. The reopening of the railway is not only related to the revenue of the Beining Railway, but the Japanese side also believes that it has a great impact on its interests and hopes to resolve it at the same time as the takeover of Shanhaiguan. Since the Beining Railway Bureau drafted a plan and submitted it to the Ministry of Railways for approval, the Ministry of Railways has taken a cautious attitude and has not yet sent a reply to Beiping. The director of the railway bureau, Yin Tong, believes that this matter has been pending for a long time, causing many inconveniences, so he went to Nanjing in person the day before yesterday to negotiate, intending to urge its early resolution and is currently negotiating with the central government.

According to Tao Shangming's conversation with reporters this morning, the takeover of Shanhaiguan is generally not a problem. Both sides have agreed on all principles, and only the time and procedures need to be negotiated. Igi, the head of the Japanese Special Service Agency in Shanhaiguan, has recently exchanged telegrams with the Kwantung Army and has probably received a reply. The takeover is expected to be implemented by the end of the year. I came to Beiping today to meet with Chairman Huang to make a concrete formulation of our intentions and will go to Tianjin in the next few days to meet with the Japanese representative Igi to discuss everything. The Japanese side has not formally raised the issue of East Luocheng. The Japanese barracks and market in that area are mostly completed and are still under construction. The provincial government is considering the issue of the Shanhaiguan Special Public Security Bureau in order to save expenses. The puppet Linyu Local Maintenance Association will naturally be abolished. The disposal of its personnel will depend on future circumstances. (14th December)

Chiang Orders Seven Provinces to Strictly Prohibit Planting of Tobacco Seedlings - Officers and Soldiers Protecting Them to be Punished by Military Law -

Hankou Correspondence: Chairman Chiang yesterday telegraphed the governments of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Hunan, Jiangxi, Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, the Pacification Commissioner's Offices of Henan and Hubei, and the military commanders stationed in the seven provinces, reiterating the ban on planting tobacco seedlings. The telegram said: (It has been found that the central provinces have absolutely prohibited the planting of opium, and measures for investigating and prohibiting the planting of opium were drafted last year and submitted to the National Government for approval, and telegrams were issued to comply with them. Personnel were dispatched in the spring of this year to investigate and prohibit them, and in September, telegrams were issued to strictly prohibit them. Now that winter is approaching, it is the time to sow tobacco seedlings, and lawless people and a few local bullies may inevitably try to do so, clinging to their old habits, instigating ignorant people, and violating the ban. If the investigation and prohibition are slightly lax, the poisonous weeds will have a resurgence. I hereby reiterate the strict prohibition, instructing all military and political commanders to strictly order their subordinates to be responsible for the investigation and prohibition, so that all the jurisdictions must be completely eradicated, and no more seeds should enter the ground and no more seedlings should come out of the soil. In remote areas, if there are any cases of resisting orders and secretly planting, the military and political commanders of the respective jurisdictions should supervise the investigation and eradication, and the planters should be arrested and punished to the fullest extent of the law, without any leniency. If any unscrupulous officers and soldiers or local bullies take the opportunity to collude and protect them, they will be punished by military law as soon as they are discovered. After this ban, if tobacco seedlings are found in any of the jurisdictions, the respective military and political commanders will be held accountable. In addition to separate orders, this order is issued to comply with and forward it to all subordinates to abide by and report the handling of the matter. This order.) (15th)

The Financial Crisis in Shantou Over the Past Year = The Course of Three Total Collapses = = The Chamber of Commerce Still Tries to Maintain It =

Shantou Correspondence: The warning of the total financial collapse of Chao-Shan was seen last winter, but the various silver firms could still try their best to support it. Until this spring, remittances from Southeast Asia were sharply reduced, and rural areas were bankrupted by the pressure of taxes. Under the double impact, business became more and more sluggish, and each item on the market was taxed several times, with taxes exceeding the cost. In addition, the cash circulating in the market was continuously absorbed by the authorities year after year. As a result, Shantou became a world of paper money, and the paper money was printed by commercial silver firms. This spring, the amount of cash was sharply reduced, and the amount of paper money gradually decreased due to the closure or withdrawal of various silver firms. As a result, the market fluctuated. The first collapse occurred after Qingming and before the Dragon Boat Festival. Dozens of large shops and silver firms closed down at the same time, owing more than 2 million yuan in front debts. At that time, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Silver Exchange Association, and others tried their best to maintain it, and agreed on joint guarantee measures, issued industrial guarantee white notes, used them in the market, set interest rates, restricted withdrawals, and prohibited silver exports. The market was slightly stabilized for a while, but there was no fundamental solution. The fundamental solution lies in the government reducing taxes to relieve the people's difficulties. May I ask, how can we rely on paper money to save paper money for a long time? Therefore, around the Mid-Autumn Festival, the white notes expired and could not be cashed. Merchants were very suspicious of them, and the credit of silver firms plummeted. The second wave of total collapse followed. Chen Yuanda, Cheng Mao, Bao Sheng, and other major silver firms, which were the backbone of the Chaozhou gang silver firms, were once again swept into the abyss by the evil waves, owing about 2 million yuan in front debts. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce struggled to take on the responsibility of clearing debts again. This wave gradually subsided. Unexpectedly, as the end of the solar year approached, the silver firms unfortunately experienced a third total collapse. The first to bear the brunt were Guangfa, Zhifa, and Hongfa, the three companies of the Chenghai silver firm, all opened by the Gao family, a wealthy merchant in Chenghai, owing a total of more than 1 million yuan in front debts. As a result, the Jiafa and other silver firms collapsed. On the 8th, Qianxingchang and Guangchengchang on Yongtai Street followed. These two firms were opened by Xiao Huichu, a Raoping native, with Qianxingchang owing more than 700,000 yuan in front debts and Guangchengchang owing more than 200,000 yuan. The reason for their closure was temporary financial difficulties. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce decided to maintain the situation: (1) Because the guaranteed banknotes and white notes of each firm have industrial guarantees, they are stamped with the words "circulate as usual" and are used as usual. They will not be cashed within these four months in order to get through the Lunar New Year; (2) Regardless of which industry or silver firm, all due bills from the 8th will be transferred for 60 days, with an interest rate of 2.5% for silver firms and 3% for other industries. Those who violate this will be punished by the government and fined 500 yuan; (3) Customers with deposit accounts can only withdraw one-tenth of the deposit amount each month. Other industries and silver firms still trade with each other as usual. The credit of Shantou's silver firm banknotes has been sharply reduced, and the post office and the Bank of China have stopped saving money. The post office and tax authorities discriminate against banknotes, so the price of cash exceeds that of banknotes by 50 to 60 yuan per thousand yuan. The Hong Kong exchange rate has also risen sharply, with a premium of 235 yuan per thousand yuan. The silver market in the business community is becoming more and more depleted, and the future is very pessimistic. (9th)

Shandong's Domestically Produced Cigarettes Hit by Increased Taxes - Tobacco Industry Asks Ministry of Finance to Withdraw Order -

Jinan Correspondence: In recent years, cigarettes have become popular. In Shandong Province alone, 30 million are consumed each year, and the number in the whole country is even more astonishing. Nineteen of these cigarettes are foreign goods. Recently, although some Chinese have engaged in the cigarette industry in an attempt to recover their rights, most are limited by capital and cannot compete with foreign goods. Shandong produces the most tobacco, and the labor is cheap. Cigarettes are manufactured locally at the lowest cost, so the selling price is the lowest, making it the only strong enemy of foreign goods for Chinese tobacco leaves. Three years ago, several cigarette companies in the city manufactured day and night, and demand still exceeded supply. The situation of development can be imagined. Foreign merchants attached great importance to it, but the tax system was changed in 1919, and the tobacco industry was greatly affected. Before 1919, it was divided into seven grades. After 1919, it was divided into three grades. Those above 540 yuan were the first grade, with a tax of 225 yuan. Those above 250 yuan were the second grade, with a tax of 56 yuan. Those below 150 yuan were the third grade, with a tax of 32 yuan (later increased by 7 yuan to 39 yuan). At that time, cigarette factories could still support it. On March 20, it was changed to two grades. Those above 250 yuan were the first grade, with a tax of 110 yuan. Those below 250 yuan were the second grade, with a tax of 55 yuan. For example, cigarettes with a selling price of 90 yuan have a tax of 55 yuan and a cost of 50 yuan. Selling them for 90 yuan is already a loss. Merchants cannot stop operating due to sales reasons and hope that tobacco leaves will fall in price to make a profit. Therefore, they have endured the pain until now. As of now, the tax rate has been increased by another 25 yuan, that is, the previous tax rate of 55 yuan has been increased to 80 yuan, and the tax rate of 110 yuan has been increased to 135 yuan. Foreign cigarettes are expensive, and adding this does not feel painful. However, the small-capitalized, domestically manufactured, mid- and low-grade cigarettes cannot support this sudden increase in tax. The nascent domestically produced cigarette industry is likely to be completely bankrupt. Therefore, the industry association held a meeting today and decided to petition the provincial and municipal governments to request the Ministry of Finance's General Taxation Department to withdraw the order. (14th)

Xuzhou: Paper Money Ready to be Recalled - Assets of Paper Money Merchants Have Been Assessed -

Xuzhou Correspondence: Regarding the Xuzhou Paper Money Tide, the various sectors have previously jointly discussed and sent representatives with the county magistrate and provincial commissioners to the province to petition, designated banks to replace the recall, seized the assets of the paper money merchants, and County Magistrate She returned to Xuzhou yesterday with the representatives who went to the province. The assessment of the sealed assets has now been determined, and the registration is not yet complete. The measures have not yet been announced, and it is predicted that the future will still be thorny.

Results of Petition

Therefore, She was ordered to quickly register the amount of paper money outstanding and report it to the province, so that the matter could be started immediately. However, the measures have not yet been publicly announced. Perhaps the money bills of the Ping Municipality Bureau will be used to replace them, and the assets can only be used as collateral and cannot be cashed. The provincial government must allocate a portion of cash as preparation to stabilize the situation. This measure will be decided before the solar new year. Because when the various paper money firms suspended redemption on December 2, the county government announced that it would be suspended for one month, and it would be fully redeemed on January 2.

Property Valuation

The property of the ticket merchants, except for public taxes related to shareholder transactions and a clear order to fully cash them out, the remaining family property has been valued. (A) Tianbaoyu: (1) Two residential properties, one on Old Daoshu Street and one south of the Electric Light Factory, valued at over 5,330 yuan. (2) One city foundation, located in Hong Temple in the northwest corner, valued at 800 yuan. (3) Three parcels of farmland, one in Wangdian in the Fifth District, one in Poqiao in the Fifth District, and one in Duanzhuang in the First District, valued at 8,100 yuan. The total value of the assets is 14,230 yuan. (B) Burenji: (1) Three residential properties, one in Fushui Well, one in Bazijie, and one south of the Longhai Ticket Office, valued at 21,930 yuan. (2) Two city houses, one on Daoping Road and one on Bazijie, valued at 12,700 yuan. The total value of the assets is 34,630 yuan. (C) Juhechang: (1) One residential property, located in Mahao Town, valued at 1,700 yuan. (2) Three parcels of farmland, one in Yanjia Mountain, one in Dami Temple, and one in Da Wangjia Mountain, valued at 6,000 yuan. The total value of the assets is 7,700 yuan. (D) Shixingchang: (1) Three residential properties, one in Zhou Dong Alley, one in Liang Ban Kang (Wan Hua Yong Pawnshop), and one south of the Prefectural Office (Hong Xing Yong Pawnshop). Except for the Zhou Dong Alley property, which is mortgaged, valued at 2,750 yuan. (2) One city house, located on Si Dao Street (Guang Chun Quan Pawnshop), not valued due to the mortgage. (3) Two parcels of farmland, one in Zhengji and one as county government public land, valued at 9,175 yuan. The total value of the assets is 11,925 yuan. (E) Yizhenxiang: (1) Three city houses, all located on Zhongzheng Street, valued at 12,400 yuan. (F) Chunquan: (1) Two parcels of farmland, one in Yuzhuang and one in Gu Mountain, valued at 40,000 yuan. The asset values of the above six companies are all less than the amount of tickets issued. However, outstanding debts have not been included and may still slightly compensate for the difference.

Registration of Tickets

Ticket holders must begin registering their tickets from the 3rd. Originally, the deadline was the 15th, but due to the tight schedule, the county government has extended the deadline by three days to the 18th. However, for remote villages, and a small number of odd tickets, even with an extension, it will be impossible to register all of them. Therefore, although statistics are not yet complete, the actual number of tickets outstanding is predicted to be higher than the number registered. In the future, when cashing out, the registered number cannot be taken as a definite limit. (14th)

Songjiang: A Little Owner of an Oil Mill Crushed His Right Arm

In the Youbang area outside the Kuatang Bridge outside the West Gate of this city, a certain Liu runs an oil mill, using cottonseed to extract vegetable oil, and the business is doing well. Initially, several oxen were used for work. Recently, sales have gradually increased, and the ox power is limited. So, in the spring, an engine was purchased and machinery was used instead, giving it to his driver. Unexpectedly, at around 9:00 AM on the 14th, the driver's young owner saw that the oil on the car was dirty, immediately took a rag to wipe it, and accidentally, the cuff was caught in the belt, crushing his right arm. People nearby saw that the disaster had already happened and quickly stopped the car, but it was too late. The family took the injured person to Shanghai for treatment that day. It is said that his life seems to be safe, but his limbs will definitely be disabled.

Taicang: Tiger Li Jing Robbery Case

Recently, in the four townships of this county, bandits have become increasingly rampant, and cases of villagers being robbed and looted are often heard. At the home of farmer Li Yaocheng in Huli Jing in the north of Shuangfeng Township, there suddenly came more than ten bandits around 11:00 PM on the 14th, speaking in mixed accents and breaking into the house with weapons. Li Yaocheng and other men, women, old and young were tied up with ropes and arbitrarily searched and looted. Thirty piculs of white rice and a pair of gold rings were looted before they swaggered away. The victim has reported to the county government and requested an arrest.

Ming Dynasty Jade Artifacts Unearthed from Ancient Tomb

In a wasteland on Fengche Hongxi in Kunshan County, there are three graves. The land was previously owned by Lu Xingru of Kunshan and recently sold to Liu Weihua of the Cemetery Church. Liu hired Wang Da from Jiangbei to cultivate the land. Wang excavated the graves, first digging the pit in the northeast corner. The pit was covered with two stone slabs, each more than a foot thick and fifty square feet wide. When the workers removed the stone slabs, a set of coffins appeared. After digging up the set of coffins, two coffins appeared, submerged in water. The coffin wood was not very large, but it was extremely strong. Wang and others believed that there must be treasure in the meticulous pit, so they opened the coffins. The corpses were not decayed, wearing yellow clothes, with their hands, feet, face, eyes, teeth, and tongue all intact. A piece of white jade was placed on the female corpse, about five inches long, with a dragon-shaped pattern engraved on it, and a round copper mirror, engraved with the words "Made in the Jiajing Year." The matter was reported to the local Public Security Bureau. The bureau considered Wang Da to be inhumane and immediately ordered the police to arrest him. Wang fled upon hearing the news. The Public Security Bureau has ordered workers to bury the tomb base.

Suzhou: Extension of Additional Land Price Tax

The Wu County government is collecting the first installment of the land price tax for the 22nd year. Since the collection began two months ago, according to regulations, a late payment penalty of 10% will be added starting from the 21st of this month. The County Farmers' Association and others have requested the county government to postpone the additional levy due to the hardship of the farmers, in order to alleviate their difficulties. County Magistrate Zou has approved the request, extending the deadline by ten days, with the additional levy to be added according to regulations from January 1st.

Additional Interval Trains on the Sujia Road

After the Suzhou-Jiaxing Highway, which directly connects Suzhou to Jiaxing, Zhejiang, opened to long-distance buses on the 10th of this month, business has been developing quite well. Now, the road management office, due to the particularly crowded passenger traffic between Suzhou and Shengze, has transported two large and small passenger buses from Shanghai yesterday (the 16th). Starting from the 18th, additional interval trains will be added to the Suzhou-Jiaxing route, with two round trips each day. The departure times from Suzhou to Shengze are 9:00 AM and 3:00 PM, and the departure times from Shengze to Suzhou are 8:00 AM and 2:30 PM. The original direct Suzhou-Jiaxing buses are planned to have their frequency increased in the shortest possible time.

Debt Case of the Shanghai Defense Corps Commander

Wang Binyan, the commander of the Shanghai Zhabei Defense Corps, mortgaged his private property to the Shanghai National Bank in the 14th year of the Republic of China to maintain local security during the Qi-Lu War. The debt has not yet been repaid, totaling 14,135.66 yuan in principal and interest. Recently, the National Bank sued the Shanghai Local Court, and a judgment was made ordering Wang to pay the full amount. Wang argued that the details of this debt had been reported to the Central Government and that the proceeds from the sale of the arsenal land would be used for repayment. He had requested the National Bank to extend the repayment date, but the request was rejected. Therefore, he appealed the first-instance judgment to the Jiangsu High Court. Yesterday (the 16th) morning, the Civil Division heard the case. Lawyer Tang Youwei and Wang Liangqing appeared in court on behalf of the National Bank, and Liu Yuanzi appeared on behalf of Wang Binyan. The judge attempted to mediate a settlement but was unsuccessful. The debate was then declared closed, and the judgment was scheduled for the 20th.

Wuxi: Arrest of a Fraudulent Recruiting Officer for Extortion

Lin Youshan from Shandong used to pull rickshaws for a living. Later, he worked as a reserve policeman in the Anti-Smuggling Patrol Team, but was dismissed due to an incident. He recently lived at No. 44 Jiang Lane on the Fourth Branch Road of Guangqin outside the North Gate of this county, living with a local woman. Recently, he has been falsely posing as a military officer and filling the role of a recruiting committee member, extorting money everywhere. Yesterday (the 16th) morning at 10:00 AM, he extorted money from Zhu Yumin, a famous doctor of traditional Chinese medicine on that road. Zhu reported the matter to the police, and they brought people from the Sixth Branch of the Public Security Bureau. After a preliminary trial by Branch Chief Duan, Yang Youshan was deemed extremely hateful for repeatedly posing as a military officer and extorting money within the jurisdiction. A special document was prepared, and police were dispatched to transfer both parties to the County Public Security Bureau for interrogation. After Officer Zhang opened the court and interrogated them, he ordered them to be detained pending investigation.

Chamber of Commerce Scheduled to Re-elect Executive and Supervisory Committee Members

The County Chamber of Commerce held its 19th joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees at 2:00 PM yesterday, chaired by Yang Shuxi. The resolved matters included: 1. Appointing Zhang Jingtang as a labor-management arbitration committee member. 2. The Commercial Research Office of the Ministry of Industry sent a business tax survey form to all counties and cities nationwide. Standing Committee member Cha Pengqian was asked to express his opinions on the case and provide a practical written reply. 3. Setting January 15th of the 23rd year of the Republic as the date for the second re-election and passing amendments to the re-election election rules. 4. Appointing 32 administrators and 18 supervisors to handle the re-election in this session. 5. The number of alternate committee members was determined to comply with Article 15 of the Chamber of Commerce Implementation Rules, which stipulates that the number of alternate committee members shall not exceed half the number of committee members. Therefore, it was decided that there should be seven alternate executive committee members and three alternate supervisory committee members, all of whom would be filled by the executive and supervisory committee members elected in this session who received the next highest number of votes.

Hangzhou: Three Kidnappers Executed by Firing Squad

The Hangzhou County Local Court found the bandits Shen Bingtang, Zhou A'quan, and Zhu Guichun guilty of jointly robbing Bao Ci Temple in Chaoshan and setting fire to Xianghai Building, causing the resident monk Zhengfa to be burned to death in the fire. Shen Bingtang was also found guilty of plotting to shoot Xu Yuanlin, a member of the Deqing Base Team, resulting in his death, and of colluding to kidnap Song Fusheng in Tou Tiaota and extort 230 yuan. Yesterday (the 16th) morning at 9:00 AM, the three criminals were taken out to verify their identities and escorted to Qingbo Gate for execution by firing squad.

Local News: Sun Ke Comes to Shanghai to Talk - Central Government Agrees with Hu Hanmin's Proposal - Will Definitely Pass Unanimously at the Fourth Plenary Session - National Unity and Concentrated Power Can Be Implemented - Yin Tong's Unauthorized Approval of Traffic Should Be Revoked and Punished

Sun Ke, the President of the Legislative Yuan, arrived in Shanghai by overnight express train from Nanjing at 7:30 yesterday. At 10:00, he met with reporters from various newspapers at his private residence on Columbia Road, stating that the central government agreed with the proposals made by Mr. Hu Zhantang in Hong Kong. Whether he will go south has not yet been decided. The details of his talk are recorded as follows:

Central Government Agrees with Hu's Plan

According to Sun, everyone can agree with Mr. Hu Hanmin's declaration on resolving the current political situation. If it is submitted to the Fourth Plenary Session in the future, it will definitely be passed unanimously. The central government not only agrees with the various items in Mr. Hu's proposed plan, but has also been thinking about implementing them for a long time. However, the method and strength are still in question. The government's power is given by everyone. Past divisions have weakened the central government's power and made it impossible to implement the plan. Therefore, to realize Mr. Hu's proposal, national unity and concerted efforts are still needed.

Sun's Trip South Undecided

Sun said that the central government intends to send him south to negotiate, which is indeed true, but it has not yet been decided. It mainly depends on the situation after Zhang Ji and other representatives return north to report, and then consider whether to go south. He also said that there have been no detailed reports from Zhang and others after arriving in Guangdong. The four representatives have now left Guangdong for Guangxi. The attitude of the Guangxi authorities is still the same as before and has not changed slightly. The term of the Chairman of the National Government has expired. Whether to re-elect was not discussed when he was in Nanjing.

19th Route Army Concentrated in Yanping

Continuing to talk about the Fujian Army, Sun said that the 19th Route Army has concentrated around Yanping. The central government has transferred a part of the bandit suppression army in Jiangxi to open up for defense. However, the war has not yet broken out. He said that the attitude of the Fujian side has eased slightly, but the facts may not be the case. The people on the Fujian side initially had no intention of repenting. Many of the Jiangxi bandits have retreated into Fujian territory, which shows that the bandit suppression military affairs are quite successful, and the alliance of the 19th Route Army with the communists also has the situation of being too big to fail.

However, it is necessary to plan in advance, so there is this request.

Yin Tong's Ultra Vires Should Be Dismissed

Finally, when asked about the Beining Railway opening to traffic, Sun immediately became furious and said that the central government has never made such a decision on the Beining Railway opening to traffic. Yin Tong, the director of the Beining Railway Bureau, conducted negotiations with the Japanese side without authorization, which is an act of ultra vires. This matter must be approved by the Legislative Yuan and decided by the Central Political Council. Even the Ministry of Railways cannot disobey the order of the Central Political Council. How dare a mere director of the bureau represent the central government? It can be said to be extremely absurd. This kind of action should be immediately dismissed from his position, etc.

French Minister Weilitun Returns to His Country Yesterday - The Consulate Holds a Farewell Meeting - Many French Citizens Participate

French Minister to France Weilitun, who will be returning to his post as minister to France, has been granted permission by the French government to take a half-year leave to return to his country. He left Shanghai yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM on the French postal ship La Rousel, accompanied by his wife and Mr. Honorat, a member of the French Senate. All the details are recorded as follows:

Consul Farewell

Yesterday afternoon was the date for the French Minister to return to his country. The French Consul General in Shanghai, Mr. Merley, specially held a farewell meeting at the consulate around 1:30 to say goodbye to the French Minister. The French citizens who came to see him off surrounded the auditorium, about 200 people, shaking hands with each other as a courtesy, and the sound of (Bon Jaur) (French for good morning) was endless. Several white-clad waiters were on the stage, each holding a plate with beer and cigarettes, so that the farewell participants could freely take and eat. The cigarette was printed with the word (Natione) (meaning Sun Yat-sen's nationalism). The yellow-black tobacco is loved by the French.

Meeting Situation

The meeting was then announced to begin. Because there were no seats in the hall, the farewell participants all stood and waited. The French love freedom, but they especially like to maintain order. The meeting procedure was also very simple and solemn, without any music or other things. First, the French Consul General Mr. Merley gave a speech at the opening of the meeting, praising Mr. Weilitun a lot, and hoping that he would return to Shanghai soon. Then the French Minister gave a farewell speech. His language was humorous, and the listeners were moved from time to time. After the French Minister finished his speech, everyone applauded. In the midst of this applause, the farewell meeting was announced to be closed.

Wharf Farewell

The La Rousel docked at the China Merchants Bureau's Middle Pier and was scheduled to start anchoring at 3:00 PM. Therefore, the French Minister and the Chinese and foreign farewell participants arrived at the pier one after another around 2:00. On our side, those who arrived included Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan Chu Minyi, Central Committee Member Li Shizeng, Jianghai Customs Superintendent Tang Haian, and Chen Shiguang, the former director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, etc. On the foreign guest side, in addition to the French Consul General in Shanghai, Mr. Merley, and the staff of the embassy and consulate, diplomatic personnel from various embassies and consulates in this port, and Mr. Wei's relatives and friends, all arrived at the wharf to say goodbye, totaling more than 100 people.

French Minister Boards the Ship

Song Ziwen, a standing member of the National Economic Council, had a very close friendship with Minister Wei. Therefore, he specially drove to the French Consulate on the Bund yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM to visit Mr. Wei and express his respect for his farewell. He also presented Mr. Wei with a silver bottle. After an hour of pleasant conversation, he left. Mr. Wei arrived at the wharf at 2:20 and boarded the La Rousel with the farewell participants. He also prepared champagne in the ship's auditorium to entertain the guests. At 2:50, the farewell participants said goodbye to Mr. Wei and disembarked one after another.

Returns to Office Next Spring

Minister Wei said to the farewell participants in the ship, I am taking a temporary leave to return to my country this time, and I will return to Shanghai around March next year to meet you again, etc. During the period of Minister Wei's return to his country, all matters of the embassy will be temporarily handled by Mr. He Berno, the counselor of the embassy. As for the signing of the Sino-French Vietnam Commercial Treaty, the French Minister will take the opportunity of this return to his country to consult with the government of that country, so that he can continue to resolve it after returning to office next spring, etc.

Yun Huifang Released Yesterday

The Supreme Court declared that the Eurasian Society was innocent. American Ship Enters the Port - Damages Nine Sailing Ships

The total loss is about 2,000 yuan. Nine ships including Yancheng sand ship Jin Yongfa, Shanghai sand ship Jin Jutai, Chongming ship Yang Changshun, Jiangbei pig ship Wang Hexing, Chen Yitai, Ningbo fishing boat Zhang Shunxing, Jin Dexing, Jin Caiyuan, and Shen Jintai, etc., were either importing fresh pigs and cabbage, or importing yellow sand and gravel, or exporting groceries. Because they were waiting for the customs to issue customs documents, all the ships were anchored within the waterway designated for civilian ships in Pudong by the Zhanghuabang Hebo Sishu in Paotai Bay. Unexpectedly, at 9:00 AM yesterday, a large American merchant ship named Steel Scientist entered the port. In order to avoid colliding with a Shaoxing sailing ship, the ship turned its bow to the east Pudong Bank. The ship's original plan was to turn its bow to the west to correct itself after avoiding the Shaoxing ship, but unexpectedly, the wind was strong and the tide was rapid at that time, resulting in a loss of driving control, and it rushed straight into the civilian ship anchorage, damaging the nine sand ships above, either damaging the bow or destroying the stern, side boards, etc. At that time, there were many cargo ships parked there, causing great chaos in the order. Afterwards, the ship reached within the high tide line and the rudder was able to obey orders, so it was able to sail to Shanghai. The ship owners who were hit afterwards reported to Xie Da, Jiang Xiangtai, Shun Jinji, He Jinji, and Runtai and other customs declaration agencies. The ship owners have jointly submitted a report to the Zhanghuabang Hebo Si to demand compensation from the American merchant ship for the losses, etc.

Marconi's Wireless Message from the Ship

Responding to New Year Greetings from Academic Organizations. Guglielmo Marconi, the inventor of wireless telegraphy, visited the Far East, first touring Japan, then passing through Dalian, the three eastern provinces, Tianjin and Beijing before reaching Shanghai. During his stay in Shanghai, he received a grand welcome from all sectors. He stayed for five days and returned to the country on the Italian ship Conte Rosso at 3 p.m. on the 12th of this month. While in Japan, he received a warm welcome from all levels of society, and congratulatory telegrams poured in from all over. Marconi temporarily hired two female typists to reply to each one, demonstrating the fervent reception of Marconi by the Japanese public. This shows their reverence for scientists and their use of this event to educate the public about the greatness of wireless technology and to enhance the scientific thinking of young students. When Marconi came to China, the reception he received was far less enthusiastic than in Japan. Fortunately, when Mr. Marconi arrived in Shanghai, fourteen academic and educational organizations initiated a grand reception, expressing their deep intentions. The organizations telegraphed a New Year's greeting via wireless. The message stated “To Marconi and his wife on the Conte Rosso, wishing you a safe journey and a Super Merry Christmas and a Unidireetiona New Year. From the Shanghai Fourteen Academic and Educational Organizations” The message, with its unique choice of words, was sent in the afternoon, and Marconi replied at 8:34 PM, via radio from the Conte Rosso, “To Principal Fang Ziwei of the Shanghai China Wireless Engineering School, and to the Fourteen Academic and Educational Organizations, I was treated with great kindness during my stay in Shanghai, and now I have received your telegram of New Year's greetings. I respectfully express my sincere thanks with heartfelt gratitude. Marconi.”

According to the International Telegraph Office, wireless telegraph service between Shanghai and Hong Kong has been available since July 1, 1929. The report in various Shanghai newspapers on the 14th that wireless telegraph service between Shanghai and Hong Kong is currently being prepared is a misunderstanding.

Representatives of Qinzhou and Lianzhou Sugar Merchants, Pang Songhui, Pass Through Shanghai to Petition in Beijing

Pang Songhui, the representative of the sugar merchants of Qinzhou and Lianzhou in Guangdong, has four objectives, is passing through Shanghai to petition in Nanjing because the Jianghai Customs arbitrarily detained and fined native sugar shipped from Beihai to Shanghai. He has been entrusted by the Beihai Chamber of Commerce, the Hepu County Chamber of Commerce, and the Qinzhou-Lianzhou Sugar Industry Guangyi Hall to carry sugar samples and a petition to Nanjing. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday from Guangdong on the Yisheng Wheel and is currently staying at the Asia Hotel. Because this matter concerns the life and death of Chinese sugar merchants and has a major impact on agriculture and commerce, reporters specially visited Mr. Pang at the hotel to ask about the circumstances. A record of their conversation follows: (Reporter) Can you tell us about the circumstances of this case? (Pang) From July to September of this year, the Qinlian sugar merchants Heli, Henghe, Longguang, Changhe, and Heyi shipped native white sugar from Beihai to Shanghai five times. Each time, they reported to Beihai Customs for inspection, which confirmed that it was purely native sugar. They paid taxes according to regulations and were released. Unexpectedly, when the sugar was directly shipped to Shanghai, the Taipan of the Jianghai Customs completely detained it, claiming that it contained 10% to 20% foreign sugar. A total of 1,560 yuan in fines and 1,957 yuan in supplementary taxes were levied. (Reporter) How does this case affect society? (Pang) The impact is extremely significant. Beihai is the main hub for the export of native sugar from the southern counties of Guangdong and Guangxi. Thirty years ago, the annual export volume often reached between 300,000 and 400,000 dan. The economic foundation of Qinzhou and Lianzhou is based on the sugar industry. Since the dumping of foreign sugar, the native sugar industry has been severely hit. In recent years, exports have almost disappeared. Fortunately, last year the government heavily taxed foreign sugar to prevent its dumping. Exports of Beihai native sugar increased from more than 5,000 dan to more than 30,000 dan. It was hoped that this would increase daily and restore the old view. Now, this case has unfortunately occurred, and the sugar merchants, who are innocent, have been fined heavily and have all suspended business. The market losses are not insignificant. This is one aspect. More than ten counties of Qinzhou, Lianzhou, etc., rely on sugar cane planting and sugar making as their main secondary industries. If the sugar industry goes bankrupt, the rural economy and public safety will be greatly alarmed. This is the second. Since the tax increase on foreign sugar, industrialists and overseas Chinese from all over the world have been planning to invest in the Qinzhou-Lianzhou industry. According to recent reports, Hong Kong sugar magnates Mo Yingyuan and Zhuang Chengzhong planned to invest hundreds of thousands of yuan to cultivate sugar cane on Xuwen Mountain in the Leizhou Peninsula and set up a factory in Beihai to refine white sugar using machinery. However, due to land rights obstacles, this has not yet been carried out. Furthermore, overseas Chinese industrialists Mr. Huang and Mr. Luo had planned to set up large-scale sugar refineries in Wuli, Bolao and other places in Ling Mountain County to imitate foreign sugar. Now, because of this case, they are all stunned and shelved. This is the third point. (Reporter) Is there absolutely no foreign sugar mixed into the Qinzhou-Lianzhou native sugar shipped to Shanghai? (Pang) Merchants mix goods to make a profit. The 24th grade of foreign coarse granulated white sugar costs 30 yuan per dan, while local white sugar only costs 16 or 17 yuan, a difference of almost double. Even if foreign sugar could be imported duty-free, the cost would still be more than 16 yuan per dan, which is the same as native sugar. Given this market situation, even if the government did not interfere, the sugar merchants would not mix it, let alone face fines and confiscation. Furthermore, the Jianghai Customs began detaining our Guangdong native sugar in April of this year. Since then, it has happened several times every month. The fines for Qinlian native sugar occurred after July. Several months passed in between. If there was punishable conduct, how could they repeatedly make the same mistake and suffer losses? (Reporter) Why is the Beihai Customs' inspection of native sugar correct and the Jianghai Customs' incorrect? (Pang) The Beihai Customs is close to the sugar production area and is familiar with the difference between native sugar and foreign sugar, so there are no misunderstandings or obstructions. However, the Jianghai Customs has never been familiar with Qinzhou-Lianzhou native sugar. The shipment of this native sugar to Shanghai is a recent event. Due to inspection errors, this detention and fine occurred. Otherwise, if Qinzhou-Lianzhou native sugar had foreign sugar mixed in, it would have been punished by the Beihai Customs first, without waiting to arrive in Shanghai. (Reporter) When your representatives first went to Guangzhou to petition, what was the attitude of your province's authorities towards this case? (Pang) Recently, our province has been implementing a three-year administration plan, paying special attention to the restoration of the sugar industry. Especially the current military and political authorities, many of whom are from Qinzhou and Lianzhou, are even more concerned about the only industry in their hometown being destroyed. Therefore, when brothers arrived in Guangzhou to petition, all authorities expressed their willingness to help. The Guangdong Provincial Government also prepared a memorandum to be taken by the brothers to Nanjing and presented to the Ministry of Finance for prompt investigation and handling in order to protect domestic products. (Reporter) What is the purpose of your representatives going to Beijing to petition this time? (Pang) The joint conference of our chamber of commerce resolved four items regarding this case: (1) Please ask the Ministry of Finance to correct the Jianghai Customs' erroneous methods of inspecting the difference between native sugar and foreign sugar. (2) Please ask the Ministry of Finance to order the Jianghai Customs to release the Beihai sugar merchants' native sugar and return all past fines and supplementary taxes. (3) Please ask the Executive Yuan to order the Ministry of Finance to order all customs houses across the country to ensure the safety of native sugar exports and imports, and not to deliberately create obstacles. (4) Please ask the Central Government to explicitly exempt native sugar from export and transit taxes, and to establish measures to encourage native sugar exports. Brothers will petition the central authorities in accordance with the above four items and will not stop until the goals are achieved.

Salt Merchants from the Four Riverbanks Petitioned the Ministry to Allow Tax Compensation for Submerged and Lost Salt

Salt for consumption in the four provinces of Hunan, Hubei, West Anhui, and Jiangxi has been supplied by Huai Salt, which is transported thousands of miles inland. This is very different from the conditions in other provinces. It was originally a government-managed, merchant-transported operation. In the event of flooding or banditry, one-time tax exemptions for transporting the tax for lost salt were allowed. However, last month, the General Audit Office submitted a report to the Ministry of Finance to abolish the old rules for tax compensation. However, the merchants believe that the tax rate on the four riverbanks exceeds double the cost. If tax compensation is abolished, then in the event of an accident, in addition to the merchant's tax loss, they would have to pay the tax for salt they don't have to those who were supposed to receive the salt. They petitioned the Ministry of Finance to cancel the original order and sent many representatives to Shanghai to appeal. Their petition stated that each salt permit requires about 70,000 yuan. The transportation route is more than 3,000 miles. Even if the tax is waived for losses, the merchants only receive a profit of 1.5 yuan per tax, excluding costs. If this loss is added, one consignment of salt would be enough to bankrupt them. As for investing in insurance, the tax on the riverbank exceeds three times the cost of the salt. Not only is it difficult for insurance companies to underwrite, but merchants also do not have the resources to pay the insurance premiums for government taxes. Moreover, Hunan riverbank insurance only covers routes above Yuezhou. The transfer to lighter boats over the 3,000 mile distance, and the Xiang River and Chuan River in Hubei, are even more dangerous routes. How can an insurance company guarantee this? If it is said that the losses are not real, then how can the investigations by administrative auditors, the attention of anti-smuggling along the way, and the eyes and ears of the local people be concealed? Moreover, merchants have capital, boatmen have their livelihoods. Who would risk trying to get lucky by acting recklessly? Even if the salt has been transported to the warehouse, there is still the risk of warehouse flooding. More than ten of the twenty riverbank warehouses in Hunan were flooded during the great flood. Under these circumstances, not only are those who have been consulted afraid to pay taxes, but even those who have paid taxes are afraid to launch their boats. It seems that they have no choice but to stop transportation together. Please allow them to continue to operate in accordance with the old regulations to ensure commercial stability and protect tax revenue.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Seriously Handles the New Cultural Bookstore's Purchase of Inferior Paper The Number of Invoices Submitted Differs Greatly from the Amount of Paper Used

After identification by the Qianye Association and confirmation by the Shuye Association, the evidence is deemed solid. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously received a report from the Qianye Association accusing the New Cultural Bookstore of using inferior goods to print and sell books such as "Strange Tales from a Chinese Studio". The Chamber of Commerce forwarded the case to the Shuye Association for investigation. The reply stated that the books were indeed inferior goods, but the bookstore was not a member of the association and asked for sanctions. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce then published the details of the case in the newspapers to inform the public. Subsequently, the New Cultural Bookstore sent a letter defending itself, stating that the paper was purchased from six paper stores, including Xingji. Seventeen invoices were attached, requesting an investigation. The Chamber of Commerce then sent the invoices to the paper industry for review. The results showed that the paper sold by Yiji and other stores was Western paper and was not inferior. However, the bookstore had recently used more than 10,000 reams of paper. The seventeen invoices totaled only 6,165 reams of Western paper and 16 reams of Kraft paper. The numbers differed greatly. After receiving the reply, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent another letter to the New Cultural Bookstore yesterday stating that the various matters stated in the association's reply indicated that the quantity of goods on the seventeen invoices submitted by your bookstore differed by almost four-tenths from the quantity of paper used up to the time this case occurred. The mixing of Japanese paper is one matter, and the discussion of using Western paper with various paper merchants is another matter. The two should not be confused. Moreover, the mixing of Japanese paper in your bookstore's book "Strange Tales from a Chinese Studio" was first identified by the paper industry and then confirmed by the book industry. The evidence provided by the legal organizations should be considered factual. In addition to returning the seventeen invoices with this letter, we hereby inform you.

Special District National Goods Sports Meet Temporary Sheds Were All Dismantled Yesterday The Fire Brigade Said They Did Not Comply with Fire Safety Regulations

The temporary commercial market of the Special District National Goods Sports Exhibition, sponsored by the China National Products Manufacturers Association, was originally scheduled to open for business yesterday morning. However, the Fire Brigade said that its lead-skin sheds did not comply with fire safety regulations and were banned. Therefore, the goods transported by the manufacturers were transported back in the afternoon the day before yesterday. Yesterday morning, the dismantling of the factory sheds began. By yesterday afternoon, they had been completely demolished, and lead skins were scattered all over the ground, which was a major blow to the national goods movement. The China National Products Manufacturers Association convened a meeting of manufacturer representatives at 5 p.m. yesterday. More than 100 representatives from 89 participating manufacturers attended. Liu Zhongying was elected chairman, and the following resolutions were passed: (1) In order to remedy the situation and make arrangements for the aftermath, the association will strive to complete the notification to the Public Concession Municipal Council within ten days. (2) Within possible limits, make every effort to open early, with New Year's Day as the latest deadline. (3) All matters will be handled by the committee with full authority. The committee will also hold a meeting once every day at 2 p.m. (4) If the original site cannot be used, another suitable location will be selected and opened on New Year's Day. (5) All news will be announced to all manufacturers in a timely manner to maintain communication. The meeting adjourned at 7 p.m.

Seriously Pay Attention to Grain Transportation

The Ministry of Railways ordered the railway bureaus to comply with the instructions. The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration received instructions from the Ministry of Railways yesterday, which stated: "The Executive Yuan issued Instruction No. 573. It was found that Chairman Chiang Kai-shek had previously sent a telegram requesting the Ministries of Railways and Communications to give priority to allocating ships and vehicles to those requesting to transport rice, to properly discuss joint transportation methods, to reduce transportation procedures, and to reduce freight rates. After the two ministries promptly discussed the matter, the ministry submitted a report on the progress of reducing grain transportation prices, which was forwarded to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. Now, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's telegram was received, saying that he was very pleased with the telegram. The Ministry of Railways' planning for reducing food prices and facilitating transportation is already thorough, and it is hoped that it will continue to supervise the implementation. As for the shipping part, it is requested that the Ministry of Communications be instructed to promptly discuss the matter in order to connect and benefit farmers and merchants. In addition to replying by telegram and issuing separate orders, it is necessary for the ministry to supervise its subordinates at all times to implement the matter seriously. Upon receipt, this case was previously approved by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek of the Nanchang Headquarters by telegram on the 1st of last month. Subsequently, in order to relieve the rural areas and regulate grain transportation, it is necessary to investigate in detail at any time. If there are reasons to reduce freight rates, they should be reported to the ministry for handling. Other items, such as giving priority to allocating vehicles, should be strictly followed in accordance with the ministry's telegram and handled seriously by the subordinates, without delay. Since the instructions have been received, it is hereby ordered that they be followed. The bureau has forwarded the instructions to the Traffic Department to comply with."

Unlicensed Crew Members Are Not Allowed to Serve

The Ministry of Communications Approved an Order to Strictly Crack Down on the Second Session of Crew Member Examinations in Shanghai. The Shanghai Marine Engineers' Association previously requested the Ministry of Communications to crack down on unlicensed crew members serving on various ships. The Ministry of Communications approved the request yesterday. The second session of crew member examinations is scheduled to be held in Shanghai on January 24 of next year. The details are as follows:

Approval from the Ministry of Communications

The Marine Engineers' Association received an approval order from the Ministry of Communications yesterday. The original text stated: "One document is submitted, requesting that all subordinates be ordered to comply with the provisions of Article 1 of the Implementing Rules of the Provisional Regulations for Crew Member Examinations, to prohibit unlicensed crew members from being allowed to leave port by means of registration. It is hereby approved. It has been found that crew members who have not obtained certificates beyond the deadline have already been prohibited from serving by the Ministry in accordance with regulations. It has been ordered to all subordinates to strictly crack down. As for the claim that they are allowed to leave port by means of registration, whether or not it is true should be investigated and verified. You should be informed accordingly. Zhu Jiahua, Minister of Transportation, December 13, 1933."

Examination in Shanghai

The Ministry of Transportation believes that the duties of marine engineers and drivers are related to the safety of passengers and cannot be ignored. Therefore, the Provisional Regulations for Crew Member Examinations were promulgated on June 1 of this year. All crew members serving on various ships must apply for examination in accordance with the law before they can serve on ships. The first examination was held in Nanjing on October 24 of this year. As a result, crew members of various ships were unable to rush to the examination due to their duties (because there are more shipping companies in Shanghai than in other places). Now, in order to facilitate the crew member examinations in Shanghai, the Ministry of Transportation has decided to hold the second examination in Shanghai on January 24 of next year.

Report on Disaster Relief in Heze, Shandong Province

The China Jishi Society, together with the Yellow River Flood Relief Society and various charitable organizations, has been handling emergency relief for the Yellow River flood disaster in Heze, Shandong Province. Previous reports have been made. Now, Director Li Yunmen has completed the distribution and returned to Shanghai, bringing with him a detailed account of the relief efforts as follows: Heze County is divided into twenty townships. Except for Chonghou, Dongping, and Yongshun, which were not affected, the five townships of Liming, Xunde, Lingsheng, Changming, and Qingqiu, being located on higher ground, suffered relatively severe damage. The people's livelihoods can be temporarily maintained, so no investigation or distribution was conducted. However, the twelve townships of Pingling, Tonghe, Xihe, Qianyuan, Gangfeng, Yiju, Linhe, Dehua, Yonghe, Baozhen, Xincheng, and Yongsui suffered more severely. Director Li personally surveyed the extent of the damage, selected staff to investigate each household, and issued tickets to the poorest residents to receive funds, using the characters "Jue," "Shi," "Fang," "Neng," and "Cheng" to represent six yuan, five yuan, four yuan, three yuan, and two yuan, respectively, in five grades. The characters "Shang" and "Xia" were used to represent one piece each of a padded coat and trousers. In total, twelve townships, five hundred and sixty villages, and twelve thousand seven hundred and eighty-six households, with thirty-three thousand six hundred and seventy-two adults and twenty-five thousand and six children, received relief amounting to fifty-five thousand and thirty-seven yuan in silver, and five thousand six hundred and ten sets of clothing. In Tonghe township, thirty-nine households received additional characters: two "Jue," two "Shi," four "Fang," twenty-six "Neng," and five "Cheng," totaling thirty-nine additional characters, due to the particularly severe disaster they suffered. In addition, temporary small relief totaling two hundred and fifty-nine yuan and eight jiao was distributed, along with forty-five thousand bottles of various medicines, dispensed according to the specific illnesses. Given the severity of the disaster in Heze, this small amount is truly a drop in the bucket.

Fortune Teller Xu Suichu Sentenced to Six Months

Zhu Hongshun, a local resident who obtained illegal property gains through fraud, owns a considerable amount of land in the western Shanghai area. Before the Shanghai war last spring, he entrusted a land license for a property located on Zhongshan Road to Xu Suichu, a fortune teller residing at the New World Hotel, to exchange it for a new license at the Municipal Land Bureau. Unexpectedly, Xu colluded with accomplices and used the license to mortgage a large sum of money from the National Products Bank for his own use. He then falsely claimed that the old license was lost during the escape from the war disaster. Zhu Hongshun and his grandmother, Zhu Tan, rashly believed him and hastily published a notice stating that if the license was found, it should be considered invalid, hoping to deny the mortgage debt. Therefore, Song Ziliang, the president of the National Products Bank, hired lawyers Xu Shihao and Zuo Detao to file civil and criminal lawsuits against Zhu Tan, Zhu Hongshun (grandmother and grandson), Xu Suichu, and Wang Yigong, who acted as guarantor. The plaintiff won the civil case. In the criminal case, except for Zhu Tan, whose interrogation was temporarily suspended due to illness, the others were summoned by the criminal court of the First Special District Court for repeated investigations. The defense lawyer did not appear in court. Only the plaintiff's representatives, lawyers Xu and Zuo, reported on time. Judge Deng Baosun ascended to the fifth courtroom and announced the verdict: Xu Suichu was sentenced to six months of imprisonment for obtaining illegal property gains through fraud; Zhu Hongshun and Wang Yigong were found not guilty; Wang Yigong's counterclaim against Song Ziliang was dismissed; and Xu Suichu's suit against Lu Quanjing was rejected.

Parricide Case Occurs in Pudong - Ji Hongwen Accuses His Elder Brother of Murdering Their Mother - Autopsy Reveals Marks on the Neck

In a shack in front of Yangjing Temple on Dongchang Road, Pudong, lived Ji Fu, an old woman from Gaoyou, Jiangsu, aged 70. She had two sons, the elder son Ji Jiangcai, aged 46, worked as a cleaner and was married to Ji He, aged 41. The younger son, Ji Hongwen, aged 30, worked as a laborer at the Malianji tile factory in Dapuqiao, western Shanghai, and did not live at home. On the 12th of this month, it was Ji Fu's birthday. She wanted to decorate the house a little since she was turning 70 this year, but her elder daughter-in-law Ji He refused and was disrespectful. They had a conflict. Ji Hongwen returned home on that day to greet his mother on her birthday, saw tears on her face, and asked what had happened. He learned of his sister-in-law's unkindness and comforted his mother. He went to buy incense and candles and then left. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 14th, Ji Hongcai suddenly went to call his younger brother home, saying that their mother had died of a heart attack. Ji Hongwen was very sad and rushed back to see his mother. He saw strangulation marks around her neck. He accused his elder brother and sister-in-law of murdering their mother and reported the case to the Third District Police Station for investigation. However, Hongcai and his wife still claimed that their mother died of illness. The police, regarding the case as an accusation of parricide, ordered their detention and instructed Yao Hongsheng, the guarantor of the 24th map, to report the case to the District Court for autopsy. Prosecutor Cao Changlin, accompanied by coroner Xuan Zhiming, went to the scene and found two fingernail marks on the neck of the deceased Ji Fu, and fingerprints on the throat, indicating that she may have been suffocated by strangulation. Ji Hongwen and his maternal uncle Fu Zhaoxi also claimed that she was injured and died. Because the case involved a serious crime with significant discrepancies, it was ordered to be sent to the Zhenru Forensic Institute for a second autopsy and ordered the police to send the defendants to the hospital for investigation. Yesterday, the Third District Police Station sent the plaintiff and defendant to the court, and ordered the guarantor to send the body to the Forensic Institute for autopsy for final determination. After a preliminary hearing in the afternoon, Prosecutor Cao ordered the detention of the defendants. The body was sent to the Forensic Institute for a second autopsy.

The Tang Jiapeng Assassination Case - Trial Concluded Yesterday - Culprits Detained for Sentencing in 20 Days

Tang Jiapeng, a native of Ningbo, also known as Ah Yu, the former manager of the Rongji Game Hall in the Great World, was shot and killed by thugs in front of the Great World at 2 AM on June 18th this year. A passerby, Wu Guangcai, was also killed by stray bullets. The police have successively arrested two suspects, Zhang Tinggui, alias Xiao Sizi, from Funing, and Zhao Guangfu, from Yangzhou, and confiscated a Browning pistol from Zhao. They were charged with premeditated murder and prosecuted in the Second Special District Court. Zhang and Zhao admitted that Wang Jinkui, who is still at large, had asked Zhou, a carpenter, to hire them to carry out the shooting. The details of their confessions have been previously reported. At the time of the incident, the police found eight bullet casings at the scene. The police's firearms technicians, after comparing the bullet casings with Zhao's pistol, confirmed that three of the casings were fired from Zhao's pistol and submitted a report to the court with verification certificates. The case was originally presided over by Judge Zhang Chaozuo, but he was transferred to the Higher Third Branch, so Judge Wu Fanglian took over. The hearing was reopened by Judge Wu the day before yesterday. (The confessions of the two defendants are the same as those previously reported and will not be repeated.) After designating lawyer Cao Lin as the defense counsel for the defendants, the court announced the conclusion of the trial and scheduled the sentencing for the 20th. The defendants were returned to custody pending the sentencing.

Robbers Attempted to Rob Tram Company - Unable to Act Due to Locked Iron Box - Company Tea Boy Also Knew About It

The Chief Inspector of the General Patrol Room, Lu Liankui, learned that a gang of robbers was hiding at No. 86 North Shansi Road, planning to rob the Shanghai Tram Company at No. 7 Suzhou Road. He immediately dispatched Chinese Detectives Liu Shaokui and Feng Zhiming, Detective Zhou Honglin and others, to arrest the following Suzhou native Ji Fusheng, Tongzhou native Zhang Asi, Nanxun native Wang Yongqing, Zuxing native Ye Shaolin, women Cao Ma, Xu Chen, and Jia Wang, a total of seven people, at the address at 6:30 PM yesterday. A pistol and several bullets were found on their persons, and two fake pistols were found under the bed in the house. They confessed that they had gone to the Tram Company at 5:30 PM to rob, but the iron box of the company was already locked, so they were unable to act. Their informant was Zhang Anbao, a tea boy from Nanxun at the company. The detectives arrested Zhang as well and took them all into custody. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the First Special Court's Criminal Court. The police lawyer, Zhang Shizhu, explained the case and stated that the police were conducting a thorough investigation, so he requested a postponement of the trial. Judge Feng questioned each defendant and ordered them to be returned to custody for further interrogation at a later date.

The Ningjing Steamer is Unable to Escape Danger - All Crew Members Dismissed - Losses Reaching Over 80,000 Yuan

The Ningjing steamer of the Ningshao Company, which ran aground at Huifengji in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, can only be salvaged next spring when the water level rises. The hull is badly damaged and cannot return to Shanghai this year. The crew, sailors, and business personnel have all been dismissed and arrived in Shanghai yesterday. According to the crew members, the loss situation is as follows:

The Cause of the Accident

The Ningjing steamer ran aground on a reef in the Yangtze River on the 24th of last month. The cause was not fog, but the many hidden reefs in the river at Huifengji. The Jianghai Customs had a lightship stationed there to warn ships. Ships going up and down the river used the light as a navigation standard. Unexpectedly, the lightship broke its anchor chain and drifted out of position that day. The captain of the Ningjing, unaware of the situation, followed the light and sailed into a cluster of reefs, causing a major accident. Afterwards, the Jianghai Customs apologized to the ship owner and towed the lightship back to its original position the next day. Therefore, the Ningjing's accident was not due to the negligence of the crew.

Damage to the Hull

The Ningshao Company has unloaded all the cargo from the steamer and sent technicians to inspect the damaged areas. They found that the hull on both sides, from the bow to the midships, had been broken and damaged by the reefs in over one hundred places, and several places were cracked. As a result, the engine room flooded. After half a month of rescue work, the damaged areas have been temporarily filled, and the accumulated water has been pumped out. However, the ship remains aground on the reef and cannot be towed into the river.

Crew Dismissed

The steamer is grounded in an area where the river water is dropping daily, making it difficult to escape danger and return to Shanghai. The company decided to dismiss the staff of the business department and the midships department first and send them back to Shanghai. Now, all fifty crew members, sailors, stokers, helmsmen, etc., have been dismissed and have taken the old Ningshao steamer to Shanghai yesterday. Their salaries were paid up to yesterday and then stopped. Only a captain and two or three stokers and sailors are left on board to guard the ship. To prevent looting, two armed soldiers have also been sent to the ship for protection.

Significant Losses

The Ningjing steamer's grounding has caused significant losses to the company. In addition to the cost of sending ships for rescue and unloading cargo, the total direct and indirect losses are estimated to be over 80,000 yuan. The loss of revenue due to the long-term obstruction of business caused by the grounding is even greater. In addition, the loss of jobs for all the ship's officers, tea boys, and sailors is also significant.

The number of students in this term has increased dramatically, and the curriculum has become more comprehensive.

If the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau can lay temporary tracks along the side of the road (from Songhu Road along Sanmin Road to the existing railway line) to allow vehicles to pass, it would greatly facilitate traffic and contribute to the prosperity of the area. It is proposed that your office submit a request to the Ministry of Railways, instructing the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau to plan and proceed. Whether this is appropriate is submitted for your approval and implementation. The Municipal Government believes that the request is feasible and has approved consulting the Ministry of Railways and instructing the two Railway Bureaus to investigate and handle it.
