The Wanshan Sinks the Luyan Steamer - Rescued Soldiers Vent Their Anger

The crew suffered severe beatings. The Sanbei Company's Wanshan steamer caused a disaster in Qizhou, colliding with the Luyan small steamer, resulting in the tragic drowning of more than sixty soldiers. The steamer has already left Hankou for Shanghai and will be able to enter the port tomorrow. However, after the accident, the crew members were severely beaten by angry soldiers, and some were seriously injured. Negotiations are currently underway. The reporter will report the follow-up information in detail as follows:

Six Crew Members Died

The Luyan small steamer was rented by the headquarters from the Xiangjiang Steamer Company. It was to be returned to the company after the transport mission was completed. The small steamer could carry more than 200 tons, and the entire crew and sailors numbered about 20. Before the collision, it was said that the Wanshan sounded a horn, but it is unknown whether the small steamer responded. When the Wanshan collided amidships, the small steamer sank instantly. All the crew members fell into the water. Afterwards, it was determined that only six members of the Luyan steamer had been rescued; the rest had drowned.

Rescued Soldiers Became Enraged

Over one hundred and dozens of new soldiers on the Luyan were asleep in the middle cabin when the sudden collision occurred. The middle cabin broke in two, so all the soldiers fell into the water. The upstream water was turbulent, so after falling into the water, they were immediately washed downstream. The more than sixty rescued soldiers were mostly those who knew how to swim, so they survived. After being rescued onto the boat one after another, the surviving soldiers became enraged and sought out the captain and others to exact revenge.

The Captain Disguised Himself and Hid

Seeing the deaths of their comrades, and some even having family and friends among the deceased, the soldiers were overcome with grief and wanted to take revenge on the captain, first mate, and duty pilot. Seeing the situation was not good, the captain, first mate, and pilot, in a moment of inspiration, each changed into the ragged clothes of the stokers and sailors, smeared their faces with coal dust, and hid elsewhere. The soldiers searched everywhere for the captain and others but could not find them, so they turned their anger on others.

The Helmsman Was Severely Injured

Since the soldiers could not find the captain and others after searching everywhere, they left behind several helmsmen, as their duties as drivers made it impossible for them to hide. Thus, the helmsmen became the targets of the soldiers' anger. All the helmsmen were beaten severely, and one was beaten so badly that he barely had a breath left. The injured were sent to the hospital for treatment after arriving in Hankou.

The Wanshan Arrives in Shanghai Tomorrow

The military authorities in Hankou, because the Sanbei Company already had personnel responsible for negotiations, allowed the steamer to sail. It has already loaded cargo and set sail downstream. According to a telegram yesterday, it will arrive in Shanghai tomorrow. The owners of the sunken Luyan steamer will seek compensation, and the families of the drowned soldiers may receive compensation.

The Communications Bank and Labor University Debt Dispute - After the Judgment - University Teachers' Union Assistance

The attitude of the Communications Bank. The Shanghai University Teachers' Union sent a letter yesterday to the Communications Bank to explain in detail the case of the National Tongji University and the former Labor University being forcibly sealed by the Shanghai Communications Bank due to a dispute over mortgage funds, and also sent a letter to the Shanghai District Court requesting a temporary suspension of enforcement. The bank is not strongly insisting on the seal. As follows:

Mortgage Lawsuit Judgment

The Jiangwan Model Factory for Vagrants mortgaged all of its land, buildings, machinery, equipment, and other real estate to the China Communications Bank in August of the eleventh year of the Republic of China (1922), signing a overdraft contract for 150,000 taels of silver. When the National Revolutionary Army entered Shanghai, the former Shanghai Political Sub-Committee confiscated and reorganized the factory into the Labor University. The Communications Bank immediately raised an objection based on its mortgage rights, demanding that the Labor University repay the mortgage funds. The Labor University consistently delayed, making no concrete offers. At the same time, they were responsible for settling all the debts owed to the factory's workers. Therefore, the Communications Bank filed a lawsuit according to law. The case was suspended for several years and remained unresolved. After the Labor University closed down, the Labor University Custodial Committee member Weng Zhilong, who is now the president of Tongji University, represented the Labor University in the lawsuit. The Shanghai District Court ruled in the first instance that the Communications Bank should seek compensation from the Ministry of Finance. The Communications Bank disagreed and appealed. The Jiangsu High Court ruled in the second instance to overturn the original judgment and ordered the Labor University to repay the mortgage. The Labor University also appealed to the Supreme Court after losing the case. As a result, the appeal was rejected, and the Labor University was ordered to comply with the High Court's judgment to pay the Communications Bank the principal and interest of 107,792 taels, 4 mace and 5 fen of silver, as well as various advances totaling 3,168 taels, 1 mace, and 6 fen of silver, along with interest until the end of enforcement. At this point, the long-standing case was resolved after three trials. The Shanghai District Court immediately opened a session in accordance with the law and prepared to seal and auction the assets.

twelve liang four qian five fen of silver, and various advances totaling three thousand one hundred and sixty-eight taels one qian six fen of silver, together with interest until the end of enforcement. At this point, the long-standing case, after the conclusion of three trials, was resolved. The Shanghai District Court then opened a session in accordance with the law and intended to immediately seal and auction the property.

Request for Commercial Assistance

A letter from the Joint Association of University Professors to the Commercial Bank of China states: "To the esteemed leaders of the Bank: We are writing to you regarding a matter recently brought to our attention by the National Tongji University Vocational High School, which is affiliated with the university. They report that a dispute between the former Labor University and your bank is about to result in a court-ordered seizure of assets by the Shanghai District Court. It is our understanding that these assets, belonging to the former Labor University, were allocated to Tongji University by the 354th meeting of the Central Political Council. The debts of the Labor University, it was decided, would be the responsibility of national institutions, and should not impact Tongji University or its educational mission. The school requests your assistance in this matter. We have reviewed the facts, and note that the transfer of the Jiangwan campus of the former Labor University to Tongji University was indeed based on a central government order. Therefore, the transfer of property rights differs significantly from standard legal precedents. Moreover, at a time when industry and commerce are declining and the rural economy is collapsing, vocational education should be actively promoted. It would be unfortunate if the debts of the Labor University were to jeopardize the success of Tongji Vocational High School. We do not believe your bank would wish to see this happen. For the benefit of both parties, we have separately petitioned the Central Political Council to expedite the settlement of the Labor University's loan owed to your bank. We now also request that your bank exercise its discretion and pursue the recovery of the loan directly from the relevant national institutions, so as to avoid further impact on Tongji and protect this remaining vocational school. This would also uphold your bank's mission of revitalizing society and supporting productive enterprises. The future of education depends greatly on such assistance. We offer this humble request, hoping for your careful consideration."

Request for Temporary Suspension of Execution

A letter from the Joint Association of University Professors to the District Court states: "To the esteemed court: We are writing to you regarding a situation involving the National Tongji University Vocational High School, which is facing a court-ordered seizure of assets related to a loan dispute between the former Labor University and the Shanghai Commercial Bank. This news has caused considerable anxiety among the school community. We understand that the Jiangwan campus of the former Labor University was allocated to Tongji University by a resolution of the Central Political Council. This transfer of property rights was based on special legal provisions and differs from ordinary debt cases. Furthermore, the Central Political Council has already decided that the Ministry of Finance should be responsible for settling the debts of the former Labor University. Therefore, to uphold national credibility, it would be inappropriate to misunderstand the principal parties and directly impact the school, causing disruption to education. We are writing to you specifically to bring this matter to your attention. We respectfully request that you consider this information and, pending a resolution from the central government, temporarily suspend the execution of the seizure order to preserve education and uphold national prestige."

Attitude of the Commercial Bank of China

"A portion of the Labor University's property is currently occupied by a vocational high school affiliated with Tongji University. Upon hearing of the potential seizure, the school fears that its educational activities will be disrupted, leading to a movement to protect the school. Petitions have been submitted to party and government authorities, and appeals for assistance have been made to various sectors of society, attracting considerable public attention. However, the Commercial Bank of China has publicly stated that the court is acting according to the principles of judicial independence and enforcing the law, which should not be opposed by anyone. The bank agreed during the previous court hearing to temporarily suspend the execution of the order on the parts of the property used by the school. The remaining land and buildings not used by the school will be seized and auctioned according to the law to protect the bank's claims while still maintaining support for education. Initially, the school misinterpreted the law, claiming the property as its own. Later, it proposed unilateral terms that the bank could not accept. The school even refused to allow bank representatives to inspect the property. The bank, which has been established for nearly forty years, has consistently contributed to industrial, educational, and public welfare causes. Now that a legal judgment has been made, the bank cannot abandon its legal claims or sacrifice the shareholders' investment. The school's opposition to the execution, while of limited concern to the bank itself, has significant implications for the entire financial sector. If creditors cannot legally dispose of collateral securing a debt, who will be willing to accept mortgages from industrial factories or public enterprises in the future? This also has a major impact on judicial principles, the authority of the law, and the movement to regain extraterritorial rights. It is hoped that the school's teachers and students will calmly consider both legal and educational factors. The bank is reportedly not entirely resolute about executing the seizure. If the Labor University can settle its debts or find other acceptable means to secure the bank's claims, or if the mortgage rights are not infringed upon or extinguished, the bank may be willing to consider a compromise."

Pudong Residents Suggest Lowering Ferry Fares

Including Adding Third and Fourth Class Seating

"A letter from Xu Zuoxun and twenty-five other Pudong residents to the Pudong Association states: Respectfully, we the residents of Pudong frequently cross the Huangpu River to and from Shanghai, and request that the municipal ferry service reduce the first and second class fares and add third and fourth class seating to alleviate the financial burden on the less wealthy. Public services should aim to benefit the public, not to maximize revenue. Therefore, anything that can ease the burden on the people and foster their economic well-being should be pursued with all effort. Benefits for the many over profits for the few. With this in mind, we must address the issue of the municipal ferry service. Since the Shanghai-Gaoqiao ferry line began operations, passenger travel has been convenient, but the high fares are unheard of elsewhere in the country, and have long been a topic of public discussion. Moreover, the service only offers special, first, and second class seating, without any third or fourth class options. This places a heavy burden on poor villagers. The rural economy has collapsed and is on the brink of ruin. The vitality of the people has not yet recovered after the January 28th Incident. This autumn, two typhoons caused enormous agricultural losses. The seawalls have not been repaired, and the devastation remains. Furthermore, most Pudong residents are farmers and laborers who come to the city regularly to sell their produce and ply their trades. They work tirelessly, summer and winter, morning and evening, to make a living. Due to the current chaos and famine, the people are poor and goods are cheap. Agricultural products are difficult to sell even at low prices, and wages are low, leaving many without employment. As a result, many struggle to secure their daily meals. The hardship caused by high ferry fares is especially acute, something those living in the city cannot fully comprehend. We have repeatedly appealed to the authorities, but our efforts have been futile. In June of this year, news reports stated that the Ministry of Railways recognized that third and fourth class train cars are primarily used by the lower classes, the masses, and should be improved. As commerce is declining and the economy is in a state of panic, it is necessary to reduce the burden on ordinary citizens. Therefore, the ministry instructed the railway administration to improve the interior of the cars and reduce the third and fourth class fares. The administration has already submitted a proposal for fare reductions, which will be announced next month. Additionally, the ministry has added fourth class tickets for travel to and from Benniu, Suzhou, Weiting, Wuxi, Henglin, and other destinations. This demonstrates the government's concern for the poor, which is admirable. The Shangchuan Transportation Company has also implemented a reduction in second class fares, benefiting the common people. They are following government orders and truly working for the people's welfare. Transportation by water should be treated the same way, but the Shanghai municipal ferry fares have only increased, with no third or fourth class seating available. In this difficult time, when the people are suffering, it is necessary to reduce the first and second class fares and add third and fourth class seating. We, the residents of Pudong, are well aware of the hardships faced by the people. However, we fear that our voices are too small to be heard. We know that your association aims to improve the welfare of our hometown, and we believe that you will speak out on behalf of the people. Therefore, we humbly submit our suggestions for your review. We request that you forward this letter to the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities, instructing the Xingye Trust Company to reduce the first and second class fares of the municipal ferry service and add third and fourth class seating as soon as possible, to show compassion and benefit the common people. We eagerly await your response."

Request for Duty-Free Release of Medicinal Alcohol

A letter from the New Pharmaceutical Association to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce states: "Our members have reported that medicinal alcohol being shipped to the interior is being detained and fined by the Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau, which claims that the alcohol has not been affixed with the required 洋酒 (foreign wine/liquor) stamp tax of $1.40 per gallon. We ask for your assistance in resolving this matter. The Ministry of Finance previously intended to prevent unscrupulous merchants from passing off alcohol as 燒酒 (shaojiu/liquor) by imposing a stamp tax of $20 per 100 catties on alcohol shipped to the interior, in addition to import duties, following the example of taxes on foreign wine/liquor. At the time, the import duty was only 4 cents per gallon in national currency. However, due to the cumbersome procedures for collecting the stamp tax, the policy was not strictly enforced, and the import duty was gradually increased. The current import duty on alcohol is now twenty-three times higher than before, amounting to 45 cents in customs gold unit, including surcharges. The market price of 燒酒 (shaojiu/liquor) is $7 per 100 catties. If alcohol were to be passed off as 燒酒 (shaojiu/liquor), it would cost $12. As unscrupulous merchants have no profit to gain, they have long ceased this practice. Pure alcohol is needed for hospital treatments and pharmaceutical compounding, and is not comparable to the luxury product of 洋酒 (foreign wine/liquor). We request that you forward this letter to the Ministry of Finance, requesting that the ministry consider that medicinal supplies are essential to the lives of the people, and instruct all local Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureaus to exempt medicinal alcohol shipped to the interior from the stamp tax and allow it to be released."

Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau Revises Inspection Regulations for Bristles, Down, and Feathers

"The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce had previously submitted and received approval to implement inspection regulations for bristles, down, and feathers, starting on October 20th. The implementation has been proceeding smoothly for the past two months. However, the inspection of pig bristles has been particularly frequent since the inspections began, and merchants have requested revisions to the inspection procedures. To meet the actual needs, the Bureau has repeatedly deliberated and has submitted a request to the Ministry to revise Article 16 of the inspection regulations. The Ministry has approved the revision and filed the changes, which will take effect on the 18th of this month. Merchants in the industry have been notified to comply. The revised article is as follows: (Article 16) The inspection fees are as follows: Camel down, cotton wool, and cashmere: 7 cents per dan in national currency. Goat hair and cow hair, etc.: 4 cents per dan in national currency. Duck feathers: 17 cents per dan in national currency. Chicken feathers: 5 cents per dan in national currency. Duck down: 1 yuan per dan in national currency. Goose feathers: 30 cents per dan in national currency. Goose down: 1.5 yuan per dan in national currency. Pig bristle waste: 8 cents per lot in national currency. Pig bristles: 30 cents per dan in national currency. The above amounts are calculated according to the municipal system of weights and measures. The minimum inspection fee per batch is 1 yuan, which must be paid in full at once. The fee is non-refundable, regardless of whether the goods pass inspection."

"戴聖鼎 (Dai Shengding), a taxpayer in the Shanghai International Settlement, had his property tax arbitrarily increased by the Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC) Revenue Office. After contacting the Taxpayer Association, the SMC was persuaded by reason and reissued a new tax bill based on the property deed. The taxpayer wrote to the Taxpayer Association to express his gratitude. The correspondence is detailed below:"

Dai Shengding's Letter

"Respectfully, I am writing regarding the Shanghai Municipal Council Revenue Office's arbitrary increase in the property tax on my residence. I requested that your association lodge a strong protest with the council. Mr. Grand, the Western director of the Revenue Office, investigated the matter and contacted me by phone at the end of November, stating that a new tax bill would be issued based on the property deed on December 1st. The excessive municipal tax for the winter season will be refunded. I am grateful for your association's strong efforts in resolving this matter. Taxpayer Association's Reply

"In response to your letter of December 10th, we are pleased to learn that the Shanghai Municipal Council has charged municipal tax based on the actual property tax amount. China Anti-Tuberculosis Association Inaugurates Membership Drive

"Mayor Wu Tiecheng and leading figures in the medical community, concerned about the prevalence of tuberculosis in China, where over ten million people suffer from the disease, a major cause of the nation's weakness, have joined forces with prominent figures from various sectors to launch an anti-tuberculosis association. Since its establishment, the association has attracted a large number of members. On the 15th, at 7:00 PM, a banquet was held at the Bankers Association to honor the leaders of the various membership recruitment teams. Attendees included Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Niu Huisheng, Wu Liande, Yan Fuqing, Li Ting'an, Zhu Hengbi, Li Dachao, Guo Shun, Huang Renzhi, Yu Qiaqing, Weng Zhilong, Xu Xinliu, Lin Kanghou, and over fifty team leaders and members of both sexes. Second Special District Court Burns Confiscated Narcotics

"The Second Special District Court, following its regular practice, burned confiscated opium, morphine, heroin, red and white pills, and other narcotics and drug paraphernalia (lamps, guns), as well as gambling equipment, which had been seized by the police. This is typically done every three months. This was the eighth such burning, following seven previous burnings. The narcotics and gambling equipment seized during the three-month period from July to the end of September of this year were scheduled to be burned yesterday. Previously, Court President Ying Shi and Chief Prosecutor Chen Beisan jointly issued a public notice and submitted reports to the Higher Third Branch Court and the Ministry of Justice, as well as sending letters to various military, government, police, and legal institutions in Shanghai, and to anti-drug associations and bar associations, inviting them to send representatives to supervise the burning. A straw shed was erected on the open space east of the courthouse, and seats were arranged. Yesterday morning, workers were instructed to move the various narcotics and gambling equipment from the exhibit warehouse to the site and arrange them in numerical order. Xiang Zhejun, the chief prosecutor of the Shanghai First Special District Court, representing the Ministry of Justice, and Tang Zaili, the chief clerk of the Higher Third Branch Court, representing the Branch Court, arrived at the court around 2:00 PM, along with representatives from various institutions and groups. They were greeted by Court President Ying, Chief Prosecutor Chen, and Chief Clerk Li Ping, who escorted them to the burning site and seated them. Then, clerks Chen Boyan and Xu Chenghuang instructed workers to move the narcotics to each representative, who verified the seals and weighed the items before setting them on fire. Kerosene and salt were added. After the narcotics were burned, gambling equipment, flower gambling, mahjong, pai gow, and搖攤 (yaotun/dice game) were burned. The burning was completed by 6:00 PM. This time, 1,358 cases of narcotics were burned, including opium, morphine, heroin, red and white pills, opium residue, and manufacturing equipment, lamps, guns, pipes, etc., valued at tens of thousands of dollars. 985 cases of gambling equipment were burned, the details of which were omitted due to the complexity of the records."

Conciliation Achieved in Housing Dispute in Tui Xing Lane

"The housing in Tui Xing Lane on Baker Road is managed by the Shanghai Trust Department of the 大陆 (Continental) Bank. Recently, due to the age of the buildings, the Fire Brigade of the Municipal Council inspected and determined that they needed to be rebuilt. Therefore, the Trust Department notified all tenants that they had one month to find new homes. All rent for November would be waived, but any outstanding rent had to be paid in full. Over thirty merchants, including Chen Jufeng, Mao Shuntai, Tianheguan, Xingfangzhai, and Renhe Tobacco Factory, formed the Tui Xing Lane Tenants Association, arguing that since the January 28th Incident, their businesses had been on the verge of bankruptcy. Although there had been a slight recovery recently, the market was still depressed, and most tenants were operating small businesses that were difficult to sustain. The end of the year was approaching, adding to their difficulties. If forced to move, it would be extremely difficult. Regarding the Fire Brigade's opinion that the buildings were too old and needed to be rebuilt, they argued that this was merely an opinion of the Fire Brigade, and there was no urgent need to demolish the buildings until formal notification from the Municipal Council. The association appointed lawyers Ma Junshuo and Li Caixia to file a petition with the First District Court, requesting mediation. Yesterday morning, Judge Tao Dejun convened a hearing for mediation. The Trust Department stated that the demolition of the dilapidated buildings was a necessary fact, which the tenants were aware of. They requested that the court order the tenants to pay the outstanding rent and vacate the premises within a specified period. Lawyer Ma Junshuo, representing the tenants, stated that they did not oppose the relocation, but it was difficult to move before the end of the year due to the upcoming holiday and the depressed market. They requested to be allowed to relocate by the end of March of next year, and to pay the outstanding rent in February of next year. After repeated discussions, both parties reached an agreement on this arrangement, and the court declared the mediation successful."

Hope for Resolution in the Kai Kai Sheng Jue Case

"Kai Sheng, the abbot of Guoren Temple, was previously sued for deprivation of freedom by his fellow monk Kai Jue from the Chao Yin Cave of Mount Putuo, who was represented by lawyers Li Mian, Chen Qun, and Dong Banggan, who filed suit in the Second Special District Court. Kai Sheng also retained lawyers Li Fengshen and Tu Zheng鵠 (Tu Zhengu) to defend him. The proceedings of the two hearings have been reported previously. Yesterday afternoon was the date for the next hearing. Both parties were represented by their lawyers. At 3:00 PM, Judge Li Changnian took the bench in the Second Criminal Court. After the lawyers entered the court, the court clerk called the names of the parties. The lawyer for the plaintiff, Li Mian, stated that negotiations for a settlement were underway and requested a postponement. If a settlement was not reached, he would request that the hearing proceed. Then, Li Fengshen, the lawyer for the defendant, stated that mediators were currently working to facilitate a settlement, and that both lawyers had agreed to attempt a settlement. He requested that the court grant a one-week postponement. The court approved the postponement and scheduled the next hearing for 2:00 PM on the 23rd, and then adjourned."

Apprehension of Robbers and Seizure of Handguns

Hua Detective Chief Su Changsheng of the Yulin Road Police Station apprehended a robber named Wang Yuezhi, a native of Chongming, at approximately 4:30 PM the day before yesterday near Huade Road and Huasheng Road. Upon interrogation, he learned that his accomplices, Cao Asi, also from Chongming, and Lu Chuanming from Haimen, were waiting inside a teahouse at No. 393 Huade Road. They secretly proceeded to the address and arrested Cao and Lu. Wang confessed that the firearms were hidden in the kitchen shed of house No. 2 Baishou Lane, Huasheng Road. They went to the house and found Teng Yan, a woman from Haimen. When asked where the firearms were hidden, she pointed to a vegetable basket. Detective Su seized two handguns wrapped in a blue handkerchief and twenty-eight bullets. He brought them, along with Madam Teng Yan and Wang Yuezhi, to the police station. The police chief ordered them to be detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin recounted the events, stating that the investigation revealed that the defendants were planning to rob the property of a milk stall on Huasheng Road. The handguns belonged to Chen Cailang, a friend of Wang Yuezhi, who committed robbery in Pudong and fled to Shanghai with the guns to evade the authorities' strict pursuit. They had previously gathered at a teahouse near the Xieqiao Bridge in the Old West Gate to discuss the plan. Wang Yuezhi and Chen Cailang were arrested near the milk stall while scouting for escape routes. Chen was resourceful and managed to escape. He requested an extension for a detailed investigation. The firearms and bullets were presented for inspection. Judge Wu Zehan questioned each defendant and ordered them to be remanded in custody for further review at a later date.

Intention to Commit a Crime: Possession of Military Firearms and Ammunition Leads to Conviction

Wang Runhe and Huang Guangqi, Hua Detectives of the Hongkou Police Station, apprehended a man named Lu Xiaodao from Tongzhou at the Hongyun Hotel, No. 564 Haining Road, and confiscated a handgun and five bullets. Lu confessed that the handgun was given to him by his master (i.e., the "Old Man") Zhang Hongtao, with instructions to wait near Jiaxing Road and kill his enemy, Er Huzi. Subsequently, a suspect named Xie Shuihong was apprehended. It was found that Xie and Lu were involved in the theft of property worth 258 yuan from Chen Wenxiang at No. 743 Tiantong Road and Qian Boqing at No. 10 Renzhi Lane, North Sichuan Road, between November 8th and 12th. They were escorted to the First Special District Court. Both defendants completely denied the robbery, and the victims could not identify them. They were ordered to be remanded in custody for a later date. Knowing that escape was difficult, Zhang Hongtao surrendered himself to the police station with a lawyer and was sent to the Third Criminal Court along with Lu Xiaodao for interrogation. The facts were clarified, and a sentencing date was set. Yesterday morning, Judge Liu Yugui presided over the court and sentenced Lu Xiaodao and Zhang Hongtao to six months of imprisonment for possessing military firearms and ammunition with the intention of committing a crime. The number of days of pre-trial detention was deducted from the sentence at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Lu Xiaodao was acquitted of the other charges, and Xie Shuihong was acquitted of all charges. Police lawyer Zhang waived the right to appeal, and they were immediately released.

Robbery on Medhurst Road

Yesterday afternoon at approximately 6:00 PM, seven robbers suddenly arrived at the residence of a certain family at No. 22 Ruian Lane, Medhurst Road, in the Public Concession. The robbers wore blue and black long and short robes, six of them carried handguns, and one unarmed robber stood guard at the back door. After entering the house, they drove the entire family into one room, shouting loudly and demanding the keys. One robber guarded them with a gun while the others searched the rooms, opening trunks, wardrobes, and dressing table drawers. After about an hour, the robbers fled with their loot. The victims then gained their freedom and rushed to check each room, finding everything in a mess. Old and worn clothes were discarded on the floor. Jewelry, better clothes, and cash were stolen, resulting in significant losses that were difficult to calculate immediately. The incident was reported to the Xinzha Police Station, requesting an investigation. The police immediately dispatched detectives to investigate and inquired about the appearance of the robbers before returning to the police station and sending detectives to pursue them in all directions.

Shi Shulian's Death Confirmed as Caused by Tram Collision

– Judge Personally Inspects the Scene of the Accident – Shi Shulian, a 16-year-old from Danyang, had recently been working as a messenger substitute at the Asiatic Petroleum Company on Avenue Edward VII. At approximately 9:00 AM the day before yesterday, he was riding a rickshaw No. 9296, intending to go to the General Post Office at the bridgehead of Sichuan Road. Unexpectedly, near the Zha Pu Road Bridge on North Suzhou Road, the south side of the road was under repair, forcing Shi to ride on the tram tracks on the north side. At that moment, tram B-24, driven by Chen Ruhang, was speeding towards him. Shi saw it but could not avoid it and was knocked down, sustaining severe head injuries. A Chinese policeman on duty at post No. 196 saw the accident and immediately sent the injured Shi to Tongren Hospital, where he died shortly after. The Hongkou Police Station received the report and instructed Detective Liang Junshan to investigate. The body was then taken to the forensic examination office on Faelun Road. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Zhang Junqing, appointed by the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctor Wei and clerk Wang Xiangyi, arrived at the office to examine the body. According to the report from Chinese policeman No. 196, "On that day, I was on duty at that location. I saw the tram traveling very fast. Because the road was under repair at this location, I immediately signaled to the driver, ordering him to drive slowly. However, he did not listen, resulting in this accident. The deceased is indeed the correct person." Chen Ruhang stated that he was driving the tram and saw the rickshaw only eighteen yards away, so he could not brake in time. His other statements were evasive. To clarify the truth, Mr. Zhang, accompanied by the Western police chief, personally inspected the scene of the accident before returning to the forensic examination office. He ruled that the deceased, Shi Shulian, male, died from injuries sustained after being struck by tram No. 24. The body was handed over to his father, Shi Fengchi, to be taken back for burial after signing a statement.

▲ Expiration Date for Dazhong Trial Wash Coupons Dazhong Laundry and Dyeing Company, located at No. 18, opposite the post office on North Sichuan Road in this city, has been keen to reorganize its business in order to popularize its solid color washing and dyeing method, and to make its contents clear. Therefore, it has issued free trial wash coupons at great sacrifice to various sectors, for trial purposes. The Shanghai New Method Washing and Dyeing Trade Association believes that this practice has violated Article 7 of the industry rules, and has repeatedly warned the company in writing, ordering it to stop using the coupons, and has also petitioned the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to handle the matter. However, in order to maintain its reputation, the company consulted the Association and requested that the deadline be the end of the lunar year. During the extended period, holders of the coupons can go for trial washes as much as possible, and the coupons will expire after that. It is also heard that the laundry and dyeing technicians hired by the company have returned from overseas and are experienced, so the products have won a good reputation in the society. In addition, Mr. Wu Yafei, director of the business department, has returned to Shanghai after going to Beijing for registration matters, and has obtained certificate No. 5073 from the Ministry of Industry. At present, he still personally presides over the affairs of the consulting, communication, research, training, receiving, and sending departments as usual. Letters to the Editor

Sir, I have just read in today's edition of your newspaper's local news section the article "Daguan Yuan Bathhouse's Chang Yuting Was Scared and Extorted by His Nephew-in-Law with Traitorous Leaflets." The article states that Chang Yuting and Wu Suqing suddenly disagreed and requested separation. Wu then visited lawyer Chen Chou and assistant Yang Guosheng to discuss the matter, negotiated with Chang, and as a result, Chang paid 800 yuan as the cost of separation. After reading this, I was very surprised. Upon investigation, our law firm has no staff member with the title of "assistant," nor is there anyone named Yang Guosheng. Furthermore, our lawyer has never handled the Chang-Wu separation case. The information in your newspaper is probably based on inaccurate rumors. I am writing to request that you make a correction as soon as possible. Sincerely, Chen Chou, Lawyer, December 16.

Sir, I have read the article "Cotton Industry Association's Dissatisfaction with the Evaluation of Cotton Standards" in today's edition of your newspaper's city news section. After investigation, it does not conform to the facts and should be corrected to avoid confusion. Sincerely, Shanghai Chinese Cotton Cloth Exchange, December 16.

Three Orders from the Ministry of Education Yesterday

▲ Allowing Students Forced to Leave Fujian to Audit Classes in Shanghai Universities

▲ Allowing Shanghai Education Bureau to Take High School Examination If Three Subjects Failed Last Year

▲ Ordering Shaanxi Department of Education Not to Hold High School Examination for Normal and Vocational Schools (Nanjing, 16th) Students from various universities and colleges in Fujian who were forced to leave school have petitioned the Ministry of Education to allow them to transfer to schools in Shanghai to study. On the 15th, the Ministry of Education telegraphed Shanghai Datong University and other schools, stating that the above-mentioned students may be allowed to temporarily audit classes in the corresponding grades. On the 15th, the Ministry of Education telegraphed the Shanghai Education Bureau, stating that students who failed three or more subjects in the second high school graduation examination of the 21st year of the Republic of China may be allowed to participate in all subjects of this year's high school graduation examination. On the 15th, the Ministry of Education ordered Shaanxi Province not to hold a high school examination for this year's normal and vocational graduates.

Overseas Chinese in the Philippines Issuing Donation for Education Lottery Tickets

Manila Dispatch The expenses of more than a dozen local Chinese schools are managed by the Overseas Chinese Education Association. The recurring expenses of the schools are 2% of the business tax of the Philippine government plus additional donations. The other schools all have special groups or theatrical performances to raise funds. It is still easy to maintain with a small number of students. The four schools under the jurisdiction of the Education Association have 2,000 students and need 50,000 yuan per year. Five or six years ago, the overseas Chinese business was smooth and could still be offset, but in recent years, business has declined, the additional donations are less, and there are even more people who refuse to pay, resulting in increasingly serious losses for the schools. After discussions between the Education Association and the leaders of the Overseas Chinese community, it was decided to issue lottery tickets to subsidize education funding. The Philippine government recognizes that lottery tickets have a gambling nature and strictly prohibits their issuance. However, because of the lack of funding, it did not object. The lottery tickets are named Donation for Education Lottery Tickets. The first phase will issue 50,000 tickets, each sold for one Philippine silver dollar, and 22,400 yuan will be used as prizes. The balance, after deducting the cost of issuance, will be used to subsidize education funding. The winning numbers will be based on the numbers drawn in the third phase of the National Government Aviation Lottery Tickets.

Local News: Shanghai Middle School Teachers' Association Holds Textbook Research Conference Yesterday

▲Resolutions to Petition the Ministry of Education and the Bureau of Education

▲Efforts to Unify Social Science Education The Shanghai Municipal Middle School Teachers' Association, Textbook Research Committee, held its first meeting yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. Yan Junxuan, He Xianqi, Chen Jicheng, Xu Zexiang, Zhang Hequn, Xu Xingchu, and Wu Zhiqian attended. Chen Jicheng chaired the meeting, with Xu Zexiang as the recorder. (2) To investigate the titles, locations, and authors of textbooks used in various subjects at various middle schools, it was resolved to request the Standing Committee to handle this matter. (3) To petition the Ministry of Education and the Bureau of Education to find ways to unify social science textbooks to facilitate teaching, it was resolved to request the Standing Committee to prepare and submit the petition. The meeting adjourned after the resolutions were passed.

Shanghai Jinan Alumni Association's Newly Elected Executive and Supervisory Committee Inaugural Declaration

▲Pledging Full Force to Expel the Vermin Destroying the Alma Mater The Shanghai Alumni Association of National Jinan University issued a declaration yesterday, stating: "Our association has been established for many years. Through the efforts of successive committee members and the support of alumni, it has achieved considerable success. We, the undersigned, are honored to have been elected by the general meeting to serve as members of the Executive and Supervisory Committee for the 22nd year. We are deeply conscientious in carrying on the past and opening up the future. We believe that our association is located in Shanghai, a city that connects China and foreign countries and is also the location of our alma mater. Considering the advantageous position we are in, although we do not formally bear the name of the general association, we cannot shirk our responsibility as the chief representatives. We dare not be insincere in fulfilling our obligations. Regarding the future promotion of association affairs, we would like to state the following before our fellow alumni and members of society:

(1) To raise funds for a fixed association venue to facilitate communication and reception among alumni. This is a major undertaking and requires the collective efforts of all our alumni to achieve success as soon as possible.

(2) To investigate and seek relief for unemployed alumni to enable them to contribute to society and fulfill their talents, thereby demonstrating the spirit of service of our alumni.

(3) To pledge full force to expel the vermin destroying the alma mater. Recently, unscrupulous individuals have spread rumors and slanders against our alma mater at every turn, and even sneaked into the campus to stir up trouble. Taking advantage of the tense situation, they intend to subvert our alma mater, with unfathomable intentions. We pledge to use all our strength to expel them. (A gentleman should fight with the devil; man does not live by bread alone.) We respectfully regard this as our guiding principle.

(4) To contribute opinions to the alma mater. The president, in his declining years, has sacrificed his spirit and material resources for the school. All our alumni should adopt a bright attitude, exhaust the wisdom of fools, concentrate opinions in this association, and contribute to the cause. This is also a help to consolidate the alma mater.

These are just a few of the major points. Other matters are still under consideration and cannot be described in detail. Our abilities are limited, and we hope that our alumni will provide guidance at any time to correct our shortcomings. At the beginning of our term, we hereby declare. Executive Committee of the Shanghai Alumni Association of National Jinan University, 22nd Year: Sun Yue, Yu Shaowu, Liu Wangsu, Li Bangshu, Kang Laiwen, Wu Baojin, Lin Qingchi, Ran Bingheng, Ping Zuren, Rao Zhuhua, Wen Wanyao. Supervisory Committee: Wang Weixun, Long Ziqiang, Wei Zhenhua, Chen Xiwu, Zeng Yifu, Jiang Shanjing, Wang Shanlu.

Letter from Tongji Vocational School Protection Association Published as Is

Once we have the facts, we will announce them publicly to dispel doubts and avoid hindering the future of our school's protection. A Major Disturbance: Victory Decided by Penalty Kick; Jinan Defeats Jiaotong 1-0; Jiaotong University Students Beat Referee After the Match

A Shout and Shen Huichun is Seriously Injured The football teams of Jinan and Jiaotong Universities met yesterday at the Jiaotong University stadium in Xujiahui. This was one of the most important matches for Jiangda Football, and the outcome was related to the loss of the championship. In addition to the students of the two schools, many football fans in Shanghai went to watch it. The two teams were evenly matched. Jiaotong conceded a penalty kick not long after the start, and Jinan won 1-0. As a result, a few Jiaotong students, unable to bear the frustration of defeat, blamed referee Shen Huichun. With a shout to hit him, Mr. Shen was immediately surrounded, and fists and flagpoles were used in conjunction, causing serious injuries. The order was greatly disrupted, which is a great misfortune for the Jiangda Sports Association. The details are as follows:

Beating the Referee

Jiaotong University is the most prestigious university in the country, but football matches at Jiangda have repeatedly experienced disturbances. Jinan had also been assaulted during a match at Jiaotong two years ago, the reason being Jinan students stealing the ball. Yesterday, Jinan went to Jiaotong to fight again, and the situation was quite peaceful, so it was thought that there would be no more storms. Unexpectedly, after the end of the match, Jiaotong students, because they had only lost a single penalty kick, were very unhappy and caused a major disturbance of beating the referee. The flagpoles and megaphones of the cheering squad were used as weapons. At that time, the whole stadium was in chaos. Poor Shen Huichun suffered an unfortunate event, and Jiaotong players did not come forward to mediate. Fortunately, a few officials rescued him and escorted him into the gymnasium. The reporter wanted to enter to visit the beaten Mr. Shen, but was blocked by a doorman, and the negotiation was ineffective. Therefore, Mr. Shen's injuries are unknown.

Sighing About It

Football matches at Jiangda have been plagued by disturbances over the years, and referees have been unwilling to take on the role. After the assurance of the Jiangda Sports Association and the authorities of various schools, members of the Chinese Sports Referees Association agreed to serve as referees for Jiangda matches again. Unexpectedly, as soon as the two sides joined hands, more problems arose, and yesterday's situation was particularly serious. After the match was over, Jinan players kicked the ball into the Jinan student stands, and some Jiaotong students rushed up to grab the ball, while some players chased and beat the referee. Later, the ball was taken back by the Jiaotong students, and Shen Huichun was surrounded by the crowd and suffered a beating. The situation was very scary. After Mr. Shen was escorted into the gymnasium by the protectors, the reporter was unable to find out what Mr. Shen was beaten or injured. The armed comrades were on the scene, unable to suppress the situation. Last year, Chen Jixiang was beaten at Fudan, and the negotiation took nearly half a year. Yesterday, Shen Huichun repeated the mistake. Referees are indeed not easy to do. Moreover, the beating disturbances that have occurred in recent years have all originated from the Jiangda Sports Association. The spirit of university sports in the competition has still failed to get on the right track. How can the Jiangda Sports Association, which includes the eight universities of Beijing and Shanghai and specializes in promoting university sports, comfort itself, and what about the Chinese Sports Referees Association and the members of the Referees Association who were beaten? As for the excitement of knowledgeable groups, if it is used to resist Japan and save the country, then China can be saved.

Misleading

The scenery of the football field is the same every year, and there is nothing to describe. Jiaotong had a drum team and a cheering squad on the scene to cheer and cheer, while Jinan only had more than a hundred students on the scene to watch. The slogans and flags were very simple. A banner with the words "Good Luck to Nanyan" was hung on the second floor of the gymnasium, and the four characters "(Bless Nanyang)" were hung on the top of the clock. There was also one on the top of the library, but the words have been forgotten. The most conspicuous thing in front of the school gate is (victory or defeat is not related to honor or disgrace), but such a conspicuous banner cannot live up to its name, and it has caused a disturbance of beating the referee. It is too (humorous).

Penalty Kick

The situation in the match was quite polite. The referee's enforcement was fair and without any problems. The linesmen were also appointed by the sports referee to be Liang Wendong and Lu Xiangqian to assist. Jiaotong kicked off first, and both sides had dangerous moments back and forth. However, ten minutes into the match, Jinan's right winger Yin Guiyi sent a high ball to the front of the Jiaotong goal. Xu Yahui rushed up to respond, but before the ball arrived, Jiaotong's Shen Guanlan had tripped Xu. The referee ruled that Jiaotong had conceded a penalty kick, which was kicked in by Xu Yahui. Unexpectedly, this ball was the key to victory or defeat. Afterwards, neither side gained anything, and Jinan won 1-0.

Brief Description of Football Skills

Jinan's forwards are not as good as Jiaotong's, but their legs are very fast, which is something that Jiaotong lacks. Gu Shangxiang is indeed the hero of Jinan, taking care of everything and making no mistakes. He has the concept of one man guarding the pass, and ten thousand men cannot pass. In times of crisis, Mr. Gu turned danger into safety. Chen Zhenxiang also worked very hard. Goalkeeper Ye Peichu is extraordinarily strong and saved many dangerous balls. In terms of defense, Jinan is better than Jiaotong. However, Jiaotong's Wang Changying is indeed powerful. Jiaotong was able to avoid losing more goals because of this gentleman. Shen Guanlan in the center is slow to move, and the ball is often snatched away by the opponent when it reaches his feet. The forward line lacks goal-scoring talents, and the attack is more frequent than Jinan, but the shots are all off target. Otherwise, it would not be difficult to reverse the situation.

A Quiet Day in the Garden; You You Barely Beats Western Merchants - Three to Two -

▲The Performance of Both Sides Was Ordinary and Unremarkable

▲Although Old, Western Merchants Can Still Rally At Times The west wind was hunting, and the sun was pale yellow. Yesterday, Western Merchants and You You met in the Yiyuan Garden for a Group A match. Fewer than 300 people went to watch, and the scene was very bleak. The performance of both sides was also very negligent. As a result, You You barely won by a score of three to two. The battle situation is described below:

Zang Lai Scores

When three o'clock arrived, the two teams chose their doors and then started the battle. You You fought westward against the sun. The Western Merchants forwards constantly harassed the You You territory. Jiang Shanjing did his best and saved several dangerous balls. Sun Tui-leg was lackluster and missed three good opportunities. Time passed quickly, like a white colt passing through a gap. At thirty-five minutes, the Western Merchants sent troops to spy. Although Zhuang Shihong had entangled with Stok twice, it was ineffective. Mr. Shi passed a foot in the distance, and Maolai got it and turned around to sweep the shot and scored first.

Qiaosheng Turns It Around

After losing a goal, You You's forwards began to improve slightly. However, the Western Merchants' center army, the inter-port tiger general Stoke, was the last line of defense, guarded by General Fapeng. Although Sun Tie-leg had the courage of ten thousand men, it was difficult to display his skills. Suddenly, Li Shiyou dribbled the ball to attack, and Xue Wu could not stop him. Kelisitai welcomed the encirclement and grabbed the ball, but it was intercepted by Mr. Sun in the middle and transferred to Qiaosheng. With a bang, Gu Tejing was caught off guard, and the autumn colors were evenly divided. After a short battle, Lemon came on the field, and both sides rested.

Shutang is Penalized

After changing positions in the second half, You You still showed no improvement. The forwards were very scattered and repeatedly missed good opportunities at close range. Sun Tie-leg shot at the goal, but it was five inches off. Chen Jiaqiu was also near the penalty spot and could not make a decisive decision. Western Merchants had suffered many disasters but were able to survive. They felt that their courage had suddenly increased. Fu Luosi dribbled the ball to the baseline and passed it to the center to catch and shoot at the door. Liang Shutang acted carelessly and unfortunately kissed the ball skin with his hand and was penalized with a penalty kick. Stok took the penalty and scored a goal, and the Western Merchants took the lead again with a score of two to one.

Final Victory

Sun Jinshun's anger and resentment overflowed his eyebrows in this adversity. Liang Shutang was also eager to make up for his mistake and switched with Jiaqiu. The forwards suddenly became active. Stoke sighed that he could not take care of everything. Lao Huang got the ball and retreated to give way to Tie Tui to go straight in. Gu Tejing's soul was not attached to his body and ran out to save the danger. Sun Jinshun's division once again made it a draw. Five minutes later, Liang Shutang, who was very ambitious, dribbled the ball deep and passed it into the middle. Zhong Yongsen was waiting to shoot, but was forced into a corner kick by the Ke defender. Qiaosheng opened the kick, and Zhong Yongsen made a great contribution in the industry. After that, You You had several fierce shots, but unfortunately none of them hit the target, and the game ended.

Jiangda Football: Daxia Wins Guanghua

There was also a Jiangda football match yesterday between Daxia and Guanghua, with Daxia winning 3-0.

Jiangsu-Zhejiang Private Secondary School Football and Basketball Tournament: Jinling and St. John's Split Two Championships

Football: Jinling Defeats St. John's to Retain Championship

Basketball: St. John's Defeats Jinling to Remain Hegemon

- Two Runner-up Finals Tomorrow -

(Suzhou, 16th Dispatch) The results of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Private Secondary School Football and Basketball Tournament, Jinling and St. John's Double Championship Finals: Jinling retained the football championship, defeating St. John's three to zero; St. John's retained the basketball championship, defeating Jinling forty-one to twenty-seven. In the matches for the runner-up, Taowu defeated Cuiying in football, and Shanghai defeated Yancheng in basketball. The runner-up finals will be held tomorrow.

Football Final: Jinling Retains Championship

Jinling's three to zero victory over St. John's: The football final between Jinling and St. John's was held at 1:00 PM yesterday. Jinling won three to zero to retain the football championship. The strengths of both sides were not significantly different; however, Jinling's forwards had a smooth connection, while St. John's center backs and forwards could not coordinate seamlessly. Every time the ball penetrated deep into Jinling's territory, the forwards were still catching up, missing many good opportunities. Xu Wenkui's missed penalty kick in the first half was also a fatal blow for St. John's, ultimately losing the championship by three to zero. The details of the match are recorded below:

St. John's Surrounded on All Sides

After the start of the match, Jinling launched an offensive, with five forwards attacking near the right, and St. John's was surrounded on all sides. Fortunately, Dong Anbang's composure was commendable, safeguarding their territory. Jinling's Chen Shikai and Lin Jianxue made two wonderful shots, both saved by Dong. He Xuequan's passes were effective, and Zhang Wenzhi could not intercept them. Chen Shikai's long shots left St. John's defense empty, creating many dangerous situations. Fortunately, Sun Baoshan rushed back to save the day, turning danger into safety.

A-kui Misses a Good Opportunity

After St. John's weathered the storm, Xu Wenkui, Chen Huitang, and Liu Mingde advanced in connection, causing some panic in Jinling. Zhao Ai touched the ball with his hand, resulting in a penalty kick taken by Xu Wenkui, but it was too inaccurate and saved by Weng Liqian. St. John's missed this good opportunity and tried to salvage the situation, launching another attack. Jinling was caught in wave after wave of attacks. Hu Chengji's cross was effective, and Zhou Lixian's header created an opportunity for St. John's. Ye Deming took the opportunity to shoot, but it was blocked by the post. St. John's missed two good opportunities and could not help but panic.

Blacky Succeeds in One Stroke

Jinling attacked, and Gong Desheng dribbled forward. Zhang Wenzhi should not have conceded a corner kick. Gong Desheng took the corner kick, and the landing point was excellent. Chen Shikai deliberately missed the touch, and Lin Jianxue calmly shot into the goal. Dong Anbang was unable to save it. Jinling thus won the first half by one to zero.

St. John's Loses Another Goal

Switching sides to resume the battle, Jinling tried to defend. Blacky retreated to the center back position. St. John's was eager to retaliate, and their defense could not help but become empty. Gong Desheng lobbed the ball into the middle. Xu Guangyao and Deng Minghai jumped to head the ball, but to no avail. Zeng Yulong launched an attack, penetrating the defense and scoring directly. Jinling led by two to zero.

Zu Xiu Determines the Outcome

Although St. John's counterattacked, the forward She was slow and ineffective. Jinling's momentum grew stronger. He Xueyao ran swiftly and passed effectively. St. John's defenders did not return in time and could not defend. Dong Anbang rushed out to intercept the ball, leaving the goal empty. Zu Xiu shot, but it was too high. After this scare, He Xueyao ran with joy, and Zhou Cheng could not stop him. He Xueyao made a high cross, and Liu Zuxiu rushed forward and scored. The outcome was decided, and St. John's suffered a惨败 (惨敗, terrible defeat) of three to zero. Jinling thus retained the championship.

▲Jinling Lineup: Gong Desheng, He Xuequan, Chen Shikai, Zhou Lixian, Lin Jianxue (down), Lin Jianxue (up) Weng Liqian, Zheng Shaowei, Liu Zuxiu, Zhao Aisheng, Zeng Yulong (up), Zeng Yulong (down), He Xueyao

▲St. John's Lineup: Wu Chengji, Deng Minghai, Zhou Cheng, Chen Yaotang, Dong Anbang, Sun Baoshan, Liu Mingde, Xu Guangyao, Zhang Wenzhi, Xu Wenkui, Ye Deming

Basketball Final: St. John's Retains Championship

St. John's defeated Jinling forty-one to twenty-seven: After competing for the championship on the football field, Jinling and St. John's competed for hegemony in the basketball court. St. John's had smooth coordination, and their attacks and defenses were well-disciplined. Jinling's bold and decisive style was unique.

St. John's Takes a Clear Lead

St. John's Chen Huitang took the lead with two points in the chaos. Zhang Peixin scored from long range, taking a four to zero lead. Chen Huitang missed a free throw. Jinling's Ma Dage made a long pass to Gong Desheng, who was lurking under the basket, and successfully scored, making it four to two. Jinling trailed by two points. Li Mingguang's long shot missed, but Xu Wenkui jumped to tip the ball in, scoring another two points. Chen Huitang launched an attack in the middle, scoring two out of two shots. Gong Desheng pulled back two points. St. John's led by fourteen to four.

Jinling Tries Hard to Catch Up

After a timeout, Jinling's Blacky went on a solo run, and Gong Desheng added the finishing touch, scoring four consecutive points in an instant. St. John's called for a timeout, but could not escape. Gong Desheng scored another point from the air, and Chen Shikai made another free throw, making it fourteen to eleven. Jinling trailed by three points. Xu Tiankui skillfully avoided Chen Shikai and went straight to the basket, scoring two points. A-kui repeated the same trick, but Chen Shikai used too much force, and Xu earned two free throws. Tong Yuchun scored from long range. St. John's led by twenty-two to eleven. Jinling's Lin Blacky ran quickly to the basket, and Ma Qingyuan launched an attack from the left. St. John's won the first half by twenty-two to fifteen.

St. John's Soars Straight Up

During the break, the football players from both sides cheered and supported their teams, creating a novel atmosphere, much like a competition, which was quite a sight to see. As the battle resumed, St. John's Xu Wenkui quickly scored four points. Jinling's Lin Jianxue secretly passed the ball twice and succeeded, making the situation equal, with each side scoring. St. John's Sun Baoshan was brought in, and Chen Huitang was even more powerful. Xu Wenkui got assistance from left and right, and Zhang Peixin secretly passed the ball, causing the score to soar. St. John's defeated Jinling forty-one to twenty-seven, retaining the championship. ▲St. John's: Fouls, Points ▲Jinling: Fouls, Points Xu Wenkui (forward): 1, 18 Gong Desheng (forward): 0, 12 Sun Baoshan (forward): 0, 0 Lin Jianxue (forward): 1, 10 Li Mingguang (forward): 2, 2 Ma Qingyuan (center): 2, 4 Chen Huitang (center): 1, 12 Zheng Yingxi (guard): 3, 0 Tong Yuchun (guard): 0, 3 Chen Shikai (guard): 2, 1 Zhang Peixin (guard): 0, 6 Total: 4, 41 Total: 8, 27 First Half: St. John's 22 points, Jinling 15 points Second Half: St. John's 19 points, Jinling 12 points

Football and Basketball Runner-up Finals

▲Football: Taowu Defeats Cuiying: The Taowu and Cuiying teams, hungry, embarked on their campaign at 11:15 AM. Their spirits were not weak. Going back and forth, neither side had the advantage. Later, Cuiying's left inner defender Shen Yongnian committed a foul and was penalized with a penalty kick, which was scored by Taowu's Chen Zhengen. The first half then came to an end. In the second half, neither side made any progress. As a result, Taowu won the runner-up final spot by one to zero and will compete with St. John's for the second place.

▲Basketball: Shanghai Defeats Yancheng: The runner-up final between Shanghai and Yancheng was held at 7:30 PM. After the start of the match, Shanghai passed the ball several times, and Yang Yuanqi scored under the basket, opening the scoring. Dai Guangjin changed the color, making it two to two. Yang Yuanqi scored one out of one free throw, making it five to two. Yang Yuanqi scored three consecutive times, and Huang Lifu also scored. Zhang Zhihong and Dai Guangjin pulled back four points, and the score was once again close. Shanghai was indeed extraordinary, and Huang Lifu was particularly agile. Although Yancheng felt not weak and followed closely, Shanghai always led. At the end of the first half, Shanghai won nineteen to thirteen. In the second half, Yancheng's momentum suddenly changed. Shanghai suffered another misfortune when Zhu Peisheng was also fouled out. Yancheng took the opportunity to attack, and the score was once again caught up to eighteen to twenty-one. On the field, Shanghai's Huang Lifu and Yang Yuanqi made contributions one after another, scoring repeatedly. Yancheng's momentum was perhaps at the end of its rope. Shanghai thus won the runner-up final spot by thirty-six to twenty-five.

▲Runner-up Finals Tomorrow: The order of the football and basketball runner-up finals tomorrow is as follows: 10:00 AM, Basketball Runner-up Final: Shanghai vs. Jinling; Afternoon, Football Runner-up Final: Taowu vs. St. John's.

Wang Zhengting, Xu Shiying, and Others Agree to Hold Charity Football Matches to Aid Disaster Relief

Due to Conflicting Schedules, Various Association Football Matches Are Scheduled.

It is Estimated That Disaster Relief Efforts Must Wait Until Next Year. Xu Shiying, Chairman of the Disaster Relief Committee, and philanthropists Wang Yiting and Du Yuesheng, considering the severe disaster situation in various areas affected by the Yellow River flood, jointly sent a letter to Wang Rutang and others a few days ago, proposing to the Chinese Athletic Association to hold football matches to aid disaster relief. Yesterday, Mr. Wang contacted the Association, stating that the time and location of various football matches this year have already been scheduled, and it is estimated that disaster relief efforts must wait until next year. The original letter is recorded below: (Respected Sirs, We recently received your letter instructing us to propose holding football matches to aid disaster relief. We have already contacted the Chinese Athletic Association. As this matter concerns public welfare, we will certainly comply. However, as the schedule of various football matches this year has already been arranged, the time and location cannot be added. It is estimated that we will have to wait until next year to begin the arrangements. We are currently preparing to convene a board meeting to make a decision. We are sending this reply in advance. Sincerely, Jingren, Yiting, Yuesheng, Xiaolai, Wenliu, Shaojue, Haian, Hanzhi, Sirs, Wang Zhengting respectfully.) It is said that after receiving the letter, Mr. Xu and others immediately sent a letter to Mr. Wang expressing their gratitude.

Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

The Key to Knowledge

— Kang Tun

No child doesn't like to (ask) questions; unless they are born deaf and mute. The world is full of wonders, and there are countless strange things we don't know. Any child, anywhere, anytime, all the things around us will spark our questions. But who can answer these questions one by one?

Not just children, even adults are often stumped by common questions. When they can't answer, they have to turn to books or ask knowledgeable people. But all the books and all the wise people can't answer all the questions in the world. So, those who love to learn tirelessly have to rely on their innate hands, senses, and brains to strive to explore the wonders of nature.

Little friends! At the very least, we should be able to recognize and understand the things in our daily lives. But in reality, that's easier said than done. Some scholars who study the heavens and the earth can tell you the volume, weight, and distance of planets in the sky, but they can't tell you how a bowl of rice gets to your mouth, or how a match burns into firewood.

We should use our eyes to see more. Not just look at the surface, but also see what's underneath. Use our minds to think more, and try to figure things out based on practical experiments. The more common and familiar things are, the more interesting, insightful, and irresistible they become as you peel them layer by layer like bamboo shoots and analyze them step by step.

Dawn Bugle

— Shi Yusheng

The bugle sound of (𠚣丫𠚣丫𠚣一) (𠚣一𠚣一𠚣丫) shattered my sleep and crushed my soul, but what I felt was not sadness or worry.

Ten thousand mountains, a thousand rivers. I flew over the rugged peaks, I crossed the surging angry waves; for my motherland, for my nation, go, go, go! How much heroism, how much excitement!

Tumbleweeds broken, grass withered, ice hard, frost white. I trampled on the thorns all over the ground, I braced my steely body; for my motherland, for my nation, kill, kill, kill! How much joy, how much generosity!

I couldn't help but jump up. The waning moon sprinkled threads of silver light; the dawn wind danced with the corners of my clothes.

The Little Pine Tree's Fantasy

— Yin

The little pine tree in the forest thought that its needle-like leaves were very ugly. It thought: (If my leaves were gold, that would be beautiful). The angel who took care of the trees knew what the little pine tree meant, and changed all its leaves to gold leaves that night. The next morning, the woodcutter saw the gold leaves on the little pine tree and picked them all off. The little pine tree sighed and said: (Gold leaves are not as good as tender green broad leaves). The tree angel then changed its leaves again. A little goat passed by, saw the tender leaves, and ate them all. The little pine tree thought: (Broad leaves are no good either, glass leaves must be good). The tree angel changed its leaves to glass leaves again. At night, the north wind rose, and the glass leaves were all blown off. The little pine tree regretted it and said: (No other leaves are as good as my original needle-like leaves). From then on, the little pine tree dared not indulge in wishful thinking anymore.

The Role of Air

— Da Zhai

Wang Er saw his mother boiling water and fanning the stove with a fan. The flames gradually rose, and after a while, the water in the pot made a sound. When he opened the lid, there were many bubbles on the surface of the water, reaching the boiling point. Wang Er's mother then tied the already burning charcoal into a jar, put the lid back on, and the charcoal went out. Wang Er saw this situation and asked his mother what the reason was for the fire starting and going out. His mother said: (Your question is very valuable. In the past, the Englishman Watt, because he saw his mother boiling water and the steam lifting the lid of the pot, was inspired and invented the steam engine, which is still used to drive trains and ships today. It can be seen that ordinary daily things contain scientific principles. People need air to live, as you know. There is a kind of oxygen in the air, which can help combustion. Fanning the stove with a fan is to send more air into the stove, so that there is more oxygen to help combustion, so the charcoal has flames. When the water has boiled, there is no need for a strong fire, so the charcoal is put into a jar and the lid is put on to isolate the air, that is, to isolate the oxygen. Without oxygen, it does not help combustion, so the charcoal goes out by itself, to be used again in the future.)

Filled a Nose with Water

— Xue Fan

My younger brother loves listening to stories the most. Once, my older sister didn't tell a story, she just spoke interestingly about the word (biology) from the textbook.

She said: Any kind of living thing in the world must have conditions suitable for survival, otherwise it would have been eliminated long ago. For example, the color of a grasshopper is similar to that of green grass; the color of a cicada is similar to that of tree bark. Therefore, it is difficult for children to catch them, so these colors are called protective colors.

Furthermore, for example, each part of our human body is also suitable for survival. Just imagine if our mouths were not horizontal but vertical, wouldn't we fill our noses with water when it rained?

My younger brother found it very interesting and giggled.

Brave Little Friend

— Xing Yi

After the sun in the west hid its light, there were only a few sparse stars twinkling in the dark sky. The children, unafraid of the darkness, ran across the small bridge in groups! (Thump!) Suddenly, a huge whirlpool arose on the water's surface, and a child fell into the water under the bridge! (Ah! Help! Help!)

At this critical moment, a brave little friend, without waiting to take off his clothes and shoes, plunged into the whirlpool in one bound. The current here was originally very rapid. However, his swimming skills were also very proficient! So, amidst the clapping and cheering of many spectators and children, he actually rescued the child who had fallen in!

Who is this brave little friend? Let me introduce him: he is Hua Dun, a ten-year-old student at Zhajiaqiao Primary School in Wuxi.

1、Ming'er and Rabbit Brother were walking outside and happened to meet Mrs. Goose.

1、2、Mrs. Goose laid an egg for him to play with.

2、3、Ming'er happily took it home and asked Piggy Mom to hold the door and watch what was inside.

3、4、It turned out to be Mrs. Goose's son! (Made by Min Tu)
