An Honest Child

— Bozhen

Min'er is a child of eleven or twelve years old. He has a rosy face, cherry-like lips, and a pair of dark, shining eyes. He plays and moves about all day long with a smile, and is quite lovable. Honesty is his virtue; wisdom is his talent.

Teachers and parents all like him and praise him; therefore, he lives a comfortable and happy life. The covers of newspapers often display four large characters: What are they? They are the four characters "(Aviation to Save the Nation)," urging people to donate money generously!

One afternoon, around three o'clock, Min'er happily carried his schoolbag and returned home with the neighbor's children. He entered the house, greeted his parents with a respectful bow, as was his daily habit.

He went into his small study, put down his schoolbag, and saw a pile of newspapers on the table. His eyes fell upon those four striking characters: "(Aviation to Save the Nation)," calling on everyone to donate money, no matter how much.

Then, a thought flashed through his mind:

(During the January 28th Incident in Shanghai last year, the enemy's planes were so fierce, circling above our heads and constantly dropping large, heavy bombs. Our people died and were injured; houses were destroyed and burned; it was so heartbreaking! We should quickly donate some money to buy some airplanes to strengthen our national defense.)

So, he quietly walked to where his mother kept her money, took a silver dollar, and dashed to the bank that was collecting donations to donate the silver dollar.

The next day, his mother discovered that she was missing a dollar and asked the family if anyone had taken it. Min'er got up from his small bed, walked out of the bedroom, and truthfully confessed: (I took it. I donated it to the Aviation to Save the Nation Association. Please forgive me, Mother.) His mother, seeing his clever and lively demeanor, was no longer angry. She picked him up, kissed him, and said: (Good child, you are truly an honest child! You are also a patriotic child!)

Strive for the Nation... for the Country

— Xishi

My dear son Aihua: Since the September 18th Incident the year before last, so many of our compatriots have joined the Volunteer Army. This kind of tragic and fervent emotion has filled the land and soared into the clouds. I think you know these things in detail.

In my heart, I had long harbored many words to say to you, but at that time, you were still young, and I was afraid you would not understand. Now that you are a little older, and especially now with the political turmoil in Fujian Province and the situation in the north still unresolved, it is necessary for me to tell you these things.

Your father died in battle during the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army in Nanchang. I have lived bleakly in this world for you. Although I have endured countless hardships, I have held onto a great hope in my heart and struggled until now. Aihua, do you want to know my hope? I will tell you plainly! (The only great hope I have for you is that you will follow in your father's footsteps, strive for the nation, and strive for the country.) Aihua, you do not belong to your parents' family; you belong to the nation and the country. I will never need you to be filial to me; I only hope that you will be filial to the nation and loyal to the country!

Your mother.

Two Mistakes

— Xu Zongjie

(I) Eating on the Road

When did Mom come back last night? She's still sleeping soundly now. Oh no! Class is about to start, and breakfast hasn't been made yet. What to do? I know! I'll take six copper coins from under Mom's pillow and buy a sesame flatbread and fried dough stick to munch on. Getting to class is important; I'll chew as I walk.

What a disaster! I ran into the teacher on the way. I couldn't swallow it down, and I couldn't hide it. I had to bite the bullet and go to school, where the teacher called me into the disciplinary office and gave me a stern lecture.

(II) Being Late

On Monday morning, I felt languid and comfortable lying in bed. How pleasant! Ding! Ding!... The clock struck nine. Oh no, this is bad! I jumped up, didn't wash my face, didn't eat porridge, grabbed my schoolbag, and ran. I arrived at school at a quarter past nine.

The teacher, with a livid face, asked him why he was so late. He could only say with a mournful face: (Mom took me to the Great World amusement park last night, and I went to bed late, so I couldn't get up early). The teacher snorted through his nose and gave him another lecture.

The Zoo

— Renwei

In a certain place, there is a zoo. Although its scale is not very grand, it has lions, bears, tigers, leopards, rare birds, and exotic animals of all kinds. Therefore, children love to linger in this fun place. Some like to watch mandarin ducks playing in the water; some like to listen to parrots mimicking speech; some like to watch lions eating. But this lion just dozes off all day long and has never been seen to move even once. In the cage next to the lion, there is a big bear. At first, no one paid much attention to it, but recently, it has grown bigger and bigger and can stand up and spin around, winning people's favor. So, the children all gather around the bear to play. The sleeping lion next to it is still lost in slumber, enjoying its sleep very much.

Variation in Living Things

— Jinxì

Today, I went for a walk in the countryside with my younger brother. When we came back, my brother said interestingly: (I saw that no two trees in the wild are the same.) I smiled.

When we got home, I asked my brother to dip his fingertips in ink and print them on white paper. He then discovered that the patterns of his ten fingerprints were all different. The whorls and loops were certainly different, but even whorl and whorl, loop and loop, were not exactly alike. At this time, I also smeared ink on my fingertips and printed them, comparing them to his fingerprints. He also noticed that the fingerprints of the two people were different.

Then, my brother understood the phenomenon of variation in living things.

A Glimpse of the Children's World

— Wenpu

The Sincere Company in Shanghai recently held a Children's World Fair. The venue was located on the fifth floor, covering a large area. On both sides of the entrance, swings, slides, seesaws, and other play equipment were placed, attracting many children. In the middle, a Santa Claus was displayed, smiling kindly and lifelike. On the left and right sides of the venue, various novel toys were displayed, some related to science, some with educational significance, and the military and war-related items were particularly realistic, such as airplanes, cannons, warships, tanks, machine guns, torpedoes, submarines, and other weapons, all complete. At the far end of the venue, there were two wire cages. One cage contained a kangaroo with bright eyes, crouching in a corner. The other cage contained birds of several dozens of species, with flowers and trees planted inside and sand spread on the ground, flying and dancing among them, their singing pleasing to the ear. Next to the cages, there was a cinema showing educational films, which were clear and watchable. After the film, there was a dance performance by Little People, comical and amusing, with many people gathered around to watch. Children came and went in the venue, like butterflies flitting through flowers, making people feel love at first sight. In the center of the venue, Horlicks Company provided milk powder. I happened to be very thirsty, so I tried it with a guest. Its appeal was quite strong. Competing with Horlicks Company was the lottery area. Guests, out of curiosity, threw in a silver coin, drew a bead, and claimed a prize according to the number. They actually won a pachinko game, worth about six or seven yuan, which could be considered a small fortune. Overall, the entire venue was filled with a dazzling array of beautiful things, truly a beneficial entertainment venue for children, which is of great benefit to the enhancement of children's knowledge. The Social Affairs Bureau has approved next year as "(Children's Year)." It is hoped that the authorities of the company will expand the layout, add more programs, and extend the duration of the fair next year so that all children can enjoy themselves. It is also hoped that large commercial establishments in various places will follow suit and further allow children throughout the country to enter paradise together.

Communication from Rural Little Friends

— Ziming

▲Opening

Dear children:

I am a person from the bottom of the countryside, unable to enjoy the prosperity of the city: But I am not willing to come and experience the prosperity of the city—perhaps it is also impossible? However, I would very much like to know the situation in the city. Before I can learn about the situation of the urban children, I should naturally first tell you about the original state of the countryside:

(Revitalizing the countryside), (reconstructing the countryside), we children are also familiar with these slogans. This must be a crucial issue; I think. Ah, fortunately! I am in an environment that has been doing rural improvement work for five years, with a very strong atmosphere of the crucial slogans that adults are shouting enthusiastically today. I have more to say about the countryside—this already improved and vibrant countryside; I will communicate with you from now on, I will report to you the scenery of the countryside, you—urban children, please also tell me about the things in the city, especially your activities!

——Our communication is now beginning; from now on,－

I wish you good health.

▲Understanding

Dear children:

Since that first letter was sent, it has actually increased a lot of spiritual comfort. Because when this letter reaches you, the thoughts that I have been carrying can also be known by you. One of the happiest things a person feels in the world is when people can (understand) each other. The ancients envied the (joy of mutual understanding). Especially in a world where human feelings are thin and everyone is suspicious; often a sharp knife is hidden in a smile, and a bloodless murder plot is woven into sweet words. (Understanding) each other in this world is even more precious! If society cannot (understand) each other, then there will be (bang bang pong pong), you cannon me gun, creating a smoggy atmosphere. Each of us children has a pure heart and a bright mind, which we must always maintain, maintain.

Let us children use our pure hearts and our enthusiasm to unite. The hearts of children all over the world are for (peace), (loving each other). Because it has already been united into a bright and shining childlike heart. What is jealousy, hatred, suspicion... these are the activities of adults, these are outside the scope.

Children! Remember: we are (people) who nakedly love (goodness)!

The end.

The Relationship Between Silver Prices and China's Price Level

(Continued from III) Written by Louis Zhang Lüluan

(IV) Can China Avoid Falling Prices?

In China, if a certain permanent price level is to be obtained with silver prices as the unit, and the silver-to-yuan exchange rate can be changed to offset price changes, it may not be impossible to achieve. However, when implementing this monetary system, the following points must be noted or prepared: (1) There must be at least a reliable wholesale price index that can represent most of China's situation. For example, the current Shanghai Index and North China Index represent too narrow a range.

(2) The amount of silver exchanged for banknotes must be changed frequently within a certain period of time. If the wholesale price index decreases by one percent, then the amount of silver that can be exchanged for each silver yuan must also decrease by one percent at the same time, so that it is the same as before the decrease. Conversely, if prices increase by one percent, the best way to offset this is to simultaneously increase the amount of silver that can be exchanged for each silver yuan by one percent at the same time, and the logic is the same as above.

(3) Regardless of the height or low of silver prices, various debt contracts or other guarantees can be formally concluded or fulfilled at any time, as the silver-to-yuan exchange rate moves in tandem with the height or low of prices, ensuring that both parties can profit or loss with no damage. This kind of currency standard can sometimes be called a commodity currency system, which is no different from a non-fixed silver standard. If you want a non-fixed silver standard to control the general price level in the country, then first, silver exports do not need to be restricted, and second, domestic free redemption of notes does not need to be sanctioned.

The price of Chinese yuan has always been based on a fixed weight of silver. If the price of silver is high, the price of goods will fall, so fixing the price level seems to be an important goal. However, increasing tariffs, heavily taxing imported goods, encouraging exports, restricting production, and estimating prices are probably all inappropriate and have little effect.

Since 1929, prices in gold standard countries have fallen sharply. The rulers have used many methods, such as those listed above, to fix this or that price, but none of the results have been as we wished. The way to solve the problem is to abandon the gold standard, because this can free the price of currency from being entangled with the price of gold. In the future, even if the price of gold rises, it will have nothing to do with the currency.

However, there are also countries in the world that are unwilling to abandon the gold standard even if their economic situation is not completely bankrupt. In the future, these countries may not be able to avoid serious social or political turmoil.

Editor's Note: Mr. Louis is a professor at the College of Agriculture of Jinling University, and Mr. Zhang Lüluan is a lecturer at the College. This article was translated into Chinese by Mr. Qiao Qiming and submitted to this newspaper for publication.

Securities and Public Bonds: Demand Exceeds Supply

▲ Market Prices Frequently Rise by Thirty-Four Cents to Sixty-Seven Cents

Yesterday at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange, although trading volume was not high, market prices frequently increased. While the rise in value was not substantial, each transaction was consistently stable. Although there were no significant developments in the current situation, the central government is striving to avoid war. The Southwest's attitude, while still ambiguous, has not yet closed the door to peace. The overall situation seems to have evolved into a state of "neither peace nor war," a state of "war without fighting." It is predicted that the future will not lead to a complete breakdown. Food: Flour Futures Experience Unprecedented Plunge

▲ Foreign Wheat Pricing Gradually Loosens, Low-Price Wheat Transactions Concluded

▲ After the opening of the flour market this morning, prices for all months suddenly experienced an unprecedented plunge. The briskness of trading and the ferocity of the price declines were truly rare. Although foreign wheat quotations were up two or three cents in Chicago and around one cent in Canada, the continuous offering of spot foreign wheat and the gradual loosening of pricing led to this situation. Initially, people felt relatively calm due to the implementation of tariffs on foreign wheat. But the market's instability was already latent. The government's wheat lending, given unfavorable foreign conditions, could no longer be dismissed. Yesterday, through Xiang Mao, one ship was sold to Fu Feng (or a rumor of two ships). The price was extremely low, as little as 4.20 yuan including tax (only 3.60 yuan excluding tax). Upon hearing this news, both factories and merchants dumped their holdings in large quantities, leading to the severe price drop. The steepest decline was in January, falling as low as 1.40 yuan, 1.075 yuan lower than the previous day. The remaining months also fell by 6, 7, 8, or 9 yuan. Later, prices rebounded one or two cents due to short covering. By the afternoon, trading slowed, and prices stabilized somewhat due to the government's wheat quotation being 1.50 yuan higher (4.35 yuan). Prices rebounded slightly by one cent. However, the atmosphere had already deteriorated, and the outlook was pessimistic. In the end, this month fell 4 cents compared to the previous day, January and February fell 5.25 cents, March fell 5 cents, and April and May fell 5.5 cents.

Flour Futures Experience a Rapid Decline as Everyone Dumps Holdings

After the opening of the flour futures market, prices for all months saw a consistent and sharp decline. Although foreign wheat quotations were up two or three cents in Chicago and around one cent in Canada, the market was wary of spot foreign wheat. Prices were already unstable at the opening. With the drastic fall in flour prices and the unconventional easing of government wheat lending, everyone dumped their holdings at once. However, the actual volume of chips on the market was not particularly high, so the price drops were not too significant. In the afternoon, due to a certain factory short covering, the prices weakened somewhat. The remaining months were generally stable, with little trading. As a result, this month fell 0.09 yuan compared to the previous day, January fell 0.03 yuan, February and March fell 0.07 yuan, and April fell 0.06 yuan. Arrivals of spot wheat were still low. Prices also fell slightly by about 0.05 yuan due to the standard's decline. Anhui wheat was quoted at 4.20 yuan, and lower-quality wheat was quoted at 0.12 yuan, totaling 400 bags, which were handled by Fu Feng.

Free Talk

Flowers and Leaves

— Zhongfang

After reading the 26th installment of "Interviews with Chinese Film Artists" (which featured an interview with Mr. Hong Shen, director of "The Iron Plate Red Tears Record"), I gained a slightly clearer understanding of a pressing issue facing contemporary progressive film artists: the problem of "flowers and leaves." In the "Interview," a certain Mr. Friend’s voice is borrowed to say:

("...Therefore, I always think this way: I painted this flower, and I think it looks very realistic, and my personality is also expressed. But others say I still have to add a few leaves, but I don't want to add them, because I think it's unnecessary.")

This is an argument for: No Leaves. The interviewee, Mr. Hong Shen, believes that ("Our works just have too few leaves"). This leans towards "Wanting Leaves." And the opinion of the author of the "Interview," Mr. Sha Ji, is (a compromise). He says:

("Needless to say, I don't agree with using pointless gimmicks to make things interesting, but the achievement of technical vividness is still very necessary. As for poisoning the theme by being too concerned with vividness, that is naturally the most foolish thing. However, adding two green leaves to the outside of the flower to make it more realistic, and more authentic, that is the true value of art.")

The essence of this "Flowers and Leaves" issue is roughly as follows. Originally, there is an old Chinese saying: "However good the peony is, it depends entirely on the support of green leaves." A single peony flower is not good-looking. It must have leaves to complete the beauty of the peony. So "leaves" here are not just for decoration, but a necessary condition for completing "the beauty of the peony." Flowers and leaves are opposing, yet complementary, not one being the subject and the other the subordinate.

The issue of "flowers and leaves" in art should also be understood in this way. The issue is not "Do you need to add a few leaves?" or "Add two more leaves." The issue is whether those leaves are painted correctly. If chrysanthemum leaves are added next to a peony flower, making it look neither like a peony nor a chrysanthemum, then that is truly "unnecessary."

If the flower is a peony, and the leaves are definitely peony leaves, then even if there are too many leaves, it will not "poison the theme." Because one peony and two leaves are of course a peony, but four or five, or even seven or eight, are still a peony, and will not turn into a herbaceous peony. When the "leaves" "poison" the flower (theme), it must be because these "leaves" and "flower" are not of the same kind. So, regarding the "flower and leaf problem" in literature and art, the first thing is to recognize that flowers and leaves are mutually needed and complementary, and the leaves are not in a supporting position. The second thing is to pay attention to whether the leaves have been wrongly matched. How do Mr. Hong Shen and the other two gentlemen feel about this?

The Death of Zhu Xiang

— He Jiahuai

Zhu Xiang was a student who studied abroad, a professor, and also a poet. He could be considered to have a considerable position in society. Unfortunately, he recently jumped into the Yangtze River and died for the sake of livelihood. It is not yet clear why he committed suicide, but according to many people's speculation, poverty was indeed the biggest reason for this tragedy. I met him once in the spring of this year at the Beixin Bookstore. At that time, I didn't know who he was, I only remembered a haggard and thin face. Later, after Mr. Zhao Jingshen mentioned it, I realized that it was Zhu Xiang, and said that he had already left Anhui University, had no proper job, and was having a very difficult life. His articles have been published very little in recent years, and poems cannot be sold for money. It is a dream to want to maintain a living by this. I heard that a magazine wanted his poems, but because he asked for four yuan a line, the editor who loved to scrape oil refused to publish them in anger. Last Saturday, I ran into Mr. Du Heng at the Modern Bookstore. He said that Zhu Xiang had entrusted a friend to write a letter to him, saying that he wanted to write articles for Modern, but as a result, he never sent them. Unexpectedly, he committed suicide in such a tragic way, which really surprised him. I didn't believe it at the time. It was only after I called Mr. Zhao Jingshen yesterday that I learned that this unfortunate thing really happened.

It seems that there is no record of this matter in the newspapers, but it is actually very worthy of attention, because its significance is not limited to Zhu Xiang alone. It is said that this poet's temperament was very proud and he thought very highly of himself. According to his imagination, a poet like him, although he cannot have any title like a foreign poet laureate, should at least be made to live comfortably so that he has the mood to write poems. But this chaotic Chinese society not only does not give him a comfortable life, but simply does not give him a life. He naturally felt this coldness. He could not recognize the society, understand the society, did not admit that a certain environment that could tolerate him and cultivate him like flowers and plants had collapsed, and did not believe that the bright and splendid period would really be realized, so he only saw a deep darkness. This fatal despair made him have no courage to live on, and made him have to use suicide to solve the inner pain.

Zhu Xiang is dead, and among the large group of intellectuals who are wandering and struggling, I am afraid that there are still many candidates who will choose this dead end with him.

Summer Palace of Revolution

— Shi Zhecun

The film (The Mad Knight Quixote), which is currently showing at the Nanjing Grand Theater, regardless of the criticisms it receives after viewing, already had an authority that caused a sensation in the global film industry during its production. This is because it is a masterpiece by Cervantes, a treasure of Spanish literature, with a screenplay by Paul, Morand, and directed by Basson, and is a film based on Massenet's opera, starring the world-renowned Russian singer Chaliapin, bringing together first-class talents in literature, music, and film.

Regarding the film itself, various newspaper film columns have been criticizing it recently, and it is expected that an opinion representing the majority of Chinese audiences will be determined. However, it seems that Chaliapin himself is easily misunderstood, because I once saw a sentence in an article criticizing the film, saying that Chaliapin was once very famous in the Russian aristocratic theater before the revolution. This sentence easily implies to readers that Chaliapin was a singer who served the aristocracy, but this is not the case.

Chaliapin was born in 1873 in a poor people's house in Ometievo Village near Kazan, Russia. His father was a clerk in the village office. When he was studying in elementary school, he was expelled from the school twice, once for kissing a female student, and once for fighting with a classmate (who actually beat him). So his father thought he was incorrigible and sent him to work as an apprentice in a shoe store in Kazan at the age of eleven.

Next to the shoe store was a bakery. In this bakery, there was a young baker who earned the least but read the most, whose name at the time was Alexei Maximovich Peshkov, and is now called Maxim Gorky, the great writer of the Soviet Union.

If Gorky had not met Chaliapin, and if the hard life of wandering later had not damaged his voice, perhaps he would not be a literary giant of the Soviet Union now, but a singer ranked second. Because when he was a baker, Gorky was not only a scholar among his partners, but also an artist who could entertain them with the best singing every day. Conversely, if Chaliapin had not met Gorky at that time, he would not have found better companions in his wandering life, he would not have been easily influenced by noble literature and art, his singing would inevitably become vulgar and become a江湖派, and thus be unknown to the world. Therefore, their friendship was of great help to their careers.

Because they could not bear the hopeless hard labor, one escaped from the bakery and the other escaped from the shoe store. The two of them wandered together in various villages. Chaliapin sold songs along the way, but Gorky dared not sing, he told stories to people. This wandering life laid the foundation for their respective arts.

According to Chaliapin himself, in a recent article published in the British magazine (The Reader) called (The Life Behind Art), he narrated that he understood from this wandering life that if a singer wants to gain a large audience, he not only needs a skillful voice, but also must make his songs (active), must (immerse) himself in his music, and must make himself (become the role he is playing).

From joining an opera troupe at the age of nineteen, earning twenty rubles a month, until the eve of the Russian Revolution, Chaliapin returned from a tour of the United States and became the pillar of the Moscow Imperial Theatre. At that time, he was indeed an artistic supplier to the nobles, because the poor simply could not afford to listen to his plays, but this was not his fault. In his autobiography published in 1927, he recorded a story that is very sufficient for us to understand him. I will now excerpt it here:

(When the Bolsheviks occupied Kronstadt, a group of soldiers and sailors came to ask me to give them a concert. I immediately agreed, but some friends advised me to refuse them.

(This is dangerous,) they said, (maybe this is a trick, they will say you are a bourgeoisie and kill you).

(Why would they kill me?) I said, (I have not offended them. Perhaps my songs will help them calm their anger.)

So I performed in a large cavalry school. About fifteen thousand sailors, soldiers, engineers, stokers and women came to listen. There was an engineer, who seemed to have heard the concert before, and when each song was finished, he shouted the French word "Bis! Bis!" (that is, the Chinese (再來一個!)

But many people next to him did not understand the meaning of this word. They probably misunderstood it as the Little Russian word "Bis". Although the sound is similar, the meaning is very different. Its explanation is (devil). So a stoker with bulging veins immediately rolled up his sleeves and shouted loudly:

(What bastard dares to scold Chaliapin, if you open your mouth again, I will knock out your teeth!)

Saying that, he sent a rather large fist up.

Seeing that they were about to fight, someone explained the misunderstanding. So the stoker, who was righteous, scratched his head and said to the engineer:

(Sorry, friend, I didn't understand.)

When I left there, I was really moved by the congratulations of those waiting outside the door. An old woman in ragged clothes looked at me and said:

(Thank you, thank you! Dear Fyodor Ivanovich (Chaliapin's name), I finally listened to your play!)

In this way, in the entire seven years of the terrible revolution, the sound of music never stopped. This may be because Russians cannot live without music. So the art under the Tsar's rule is still art under the Soviet rule.) From this story, we can know that Chaliapin, the artist, is not only for the nobles, nor only for the common people, he should be said to be for humanity. At the same time, we can also appreciate that as long as it is pure art, whether under the Tsar or the Soviets, it is always the same.

Two Brothers (61)

— Written by Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

They shut their mouths. He thought she would be flustered, but he didn't expect her to be so calm. He had expected some flattering and lovely gestures, some rejections that indicated consent. He had expected to stage a witty comedy of love while catching shrimp in the rippling water! But now it's over. He felt that he had only said twenty words and they were already united, already married. Since they both agreed, then they had nothing more to say. Now they both felt a little embarrassed about everything that had happened so quickly, even a little ashamed. They dared not speak again, dared not catch shrimp again, and simply didn't know what to do.

Old Man Roland's voice saved them:

(Come here, come here, children! Come and see Bo Bao Ru. He has caught all the shrimp in the sea, this guy.)

Captain Bo Qi Ru's shrimp fishing results were really excellent. He soaked his waist in the water, from this mud to that mud, and recognized the best place at a glance. Then, with his shrimp net, he searched all the shrimp nests hidden under the seaweed with a calm and accurate movement.

And those beautiful, transparent, grayish-brown sea shrimp were jumping in his palm when he threw them into the back basket with a neat gesture.

Mrs. Lu Zui Mi was surprised and happy, and never left him again, trying her best to imitate him, almost forgetting what she had allowed and the Jean who was dreaming behind her. She was just wholeheartedly immersed in the childlike joy of scooping up sea shrimp from under the floating grass. Roland suddenly shouted:

(Look, Mrs. Roland has run to us.)

She and Bier originally stayed on the shipwreck alone, because neither of them had the desire to run to the reef or search in the pool. But they hesitated to stay together. She was afraid of him, and her son was also afraid of her and himself, afraid of his own uncontrollable cruelty.

Later, they finally sat very close to each other on the sandy beach.

The two of them, together in the summer heat that had been softened by the sea breeze, faced the vast and peaceful horizon of the blue sea water shimmering with silver light, and thought at the same time: (If it had been before, how comfortable the weather would have been in this place!) She dared not speak to Bier, she knew he would give her a cold answer. He also dared not talk to his mother, he knew that he would involuntarily say something fierce.

He trampled on the round pebbles with the tip of his stick. He turned them and struck them. She, with her eyes blurred, grabbed three or four stones in her hand, and passed them from this hand to that hand with a steady and slow mechanical gesture. Then, her erratic gaze, which was wandering forward, saw her son catching shrimp with Mrs. Lu in the seaweed. So she followed them with her eyes, peeking at their movements. With her mother's instinct, she vaguely understood that they had not exchanged a word as usual. When they were watching on the water, she saw them bending over side by side. When they probed their hearts, she saw them standing face to face. Then she saw them climb the reef and sit on it to make a marriage contract.

Their images were very clearly floating in the background between the water and the sky where it seemed that only the two of them were. Their images, in this vast expanse of sky, sea, and shore, showed a kind of great aura and seemed to symbolize something.

Bier also saw them, and a dry laugh suddenly came from his lips.

Roland's code: did not turn around, but she asked him:

(What's wrong with you?)

He always mocked and laughed:

(I'm learning. I now understand how people are preparing to become turtles.)

Ye Yuman Tastes

The Biggest Feeling After Reading This Special Issue

— Gongpu

After we decided to publish these three special issues on Esperanto, we divided the content of the special issues into three aspects, namely:

(1) A brief history and general overview of the Esperanto movement; (2) The status of Esperanto in today's international community; (3) The situation of the Esperanto movement in various parts of China. When the reporter was editing and reviewing this issue's manuscripts describing the situation of the Esperanto movement in various parts of China, we could clearly see that the level of the Esperanto movement in China, except for Shanghai, Beijing, Guangzhou, etc., which were slightly energetic, most of the inland provinces were still in a rare situation. Of course, this is not enough to worry about the future of the Esperanto movement, because the seriousness of this phenomenon is a reflection of the general low level of Chinese culture. We see the general sluggishness of the publishing industry across the country, and know that most Chinese people are so indifferent to books and newspapers in their own language, and it is only natural that they have no time to pay attention to (Esperanto). However, culture is a representative of a nation. If culture is declining day by day, it means that the vitality of this nation must also be weakening day by day. Therefore, anyone engaged in the movement to revive the nation must first pay attention to the work of reviving culture. Only when culture is revived can the nation have vitality, and only a vital nation can have the spirit of revolution. We silently observe that most of the Chinese people today are still living in a situation of complacency under the multiple oppressions of natural disasters, man-made disasters, and the political and economic aggression of imperialism. We deeply feel that the success of the Chinese national revolution is still far away! Those engaged in the Esperanto movement will naturally encounter extraordinary difficulties in this environment, but the part of the responsibility they bear for reviving culture is therefore particularly increased. This is the biggest feeling that the reporter has after reading about the situation of the Esperanto movement in China. What do you think, scholars of Esperanto?

The Esperanto Movement in China: The World Movement in Peiping

— Zhong Tianqi

Around the early years of the Republic of China, an (Esperanto Training Institute) appeared near Shuncheng Root Yuane School in Beijing. The host was Jin Mengchang and the teacher was Wu Tianmin. Although the class only lasted for one month, there were seventy or eighty students. It is said that this was the first Esperanto movement in Peiping. Not long after, Cai Yuanpei became Minister of Education, and the Esperanto movement in Beijing, under the advocacy of the Ministry of Education, made great progress. Therefore, the (Esperanto Training Institute) of Yuane School developed from (privately run) to (officially run). The red seal (Esperanto Specialized School Affiliated to the Ministry of Education) is still in the library of Peking University.

At that time, the organization of the Esperanto Society of Peking University also became active. Peking University added Esperanto courses, and teachers Sun Mizhang and Russian blind poet Ero Shenke both lectured at Peking University. The current Peking University Press can still buy several Esperanto reading materials at that time.

In this initial movement, it is worth noting that a celebration meeting for Zamenhof's birthday was held in the auditorium of the Third Court of Peking University. More than 1,000 people attended this grand meeting. Important people who attended the meeting included Liu Chunlin, representative of the President, Shen Buzhou, Vice Minister of Education, and Gu Weijun, Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs. Sherishev, Sun Guozhang, and Ero Shenke gave speeches in Esperanto.

Hu Jingyi, the former commander of the Second National Army, was a person who was enthusiastic about Esperanto. The (Esperanto Specialized School) in Mengrui Hutong was opened in the eighth and ninth years of the Republic of China with the support of Hu. The teachers were Feng Shengsan, Sherishev, and Chen Shenshu. At that time, there were quite a few talents, and the teaching results were also good. Wang Xizhou, who is now in charge of the Esperanto movement in Suiyuan, graduated from this school. However, the school was closed due to political changes.

In the early days, the Esperanto movement in Peiping relied on the promotion of the Ministry of Education and other superiors on the one hand, and on the other hand, it was also due to the urgent demand for Esperanto from the society and the resonance with the ideals of human peace and equality. Otherwise, it would never have become a movement.

After the September 18th Incident, with the rise of the anti-imperialist and anti-Japanese movement, the Esperanto movement in Peiping also flourished again. Peking University first established a training class, and other schools also established Esperanto societies.

In January 1932, the (Peiping Esperanto League) was established. In their declaration, they said: (In order to truly liberate ourselves from the oppressed position, we must obtain a link to communicate between nations and increase the weapons of mass culture.)

In addition, there is also the (Peiping Esperanto Society Federation), which is the guiding and unifying organization of the Esperanto societies of various schools, and sends lecturers to teach in various places. For example, Peking University, Normal University, China College, Chaoyang College, Peiping Normal University, Women's College, Women's No. 1 Middle School, Yijiao Girls' Middle School, Agricultural College, Engineering College, Tsinghua University, Anzhong, Salt Affairs, Police High School, Business College...etc., all schools have opened classes to teach. In particular, Peking University and Normal University have opened seven primary classes each, with an average of more than 30 students each time. Advanced classes have been opened once each.

Peiping from 1932 to 1933, like Shanghai, was one of the two major pillars of the Esperanto movement in China, full of lively and new atmosphere. This year, Peiping Esperanto speakers, in view of the fact that the (Society Federation) is only the general association of Esperanto groups of students from various schools, and social people cannot participate, in order to eliminate this shortcoming, they established the (Preparatory Committee of the Peiping Esperanto Association), and actively promoted the Esperanto movement in Peiping. A supplement (The Light of Esperanto) was published in the famous newspaper in North China, (The World Daily), which is published every Friday. Since the weekly was founded on June 23 this year, it has been published for more than 20 issues.

Obviously, Peiping is currently the center of the Esperanto movement in North China, and its future is full of hope. The general public in Peiping also has a good understanding of Esperanto. Many books and magazines have abandoned English and used Esperanto subtitles instead. (The World Daily)'s 1934 calendar also uses Esperanto to mark the months and weeks. The newspapers in Peiping are very welcome to publish articles related to Esperanto. And other places in North China, stimulated by the progress of the Esperanto movement in Peiping, are also beginning to become active. The recent establishment of the (Esperanto Society of Peiyang University) in Tianjin is one example. From these facts, we can know that the Esperanto movement in Peiping not only has a great future, but also has great significance for the entire Esperanto movement in China.

Special Discussion on Esperanto

A Review and Prospect of the Esperanto Movement in China

— Jing Zhaoxin

The Esperanto movement has a history of almost thirty years in China. These thirty years of history can be divided into three periods; from the beginning to 1914, it can be said to be a (utopian period). At that time, the predecessors who advocated Esperanto were mostly obsessed with the (internal ideal) of Zamenhof, the founder of Esperanto, and enthusiastically promoted the Esperanto movement as a religion. The spirit and perseverance of these pioneers are admirable, but they idealized Esperanto too much, thinking that they could obtain the shadows of peace and friendship from Esperanto itself, but separated the Esperanto movement from realistic problems. This is the shortcoming of the early Esperanto movement.

The World War broke out in 1914, and Chinese politics also entered a dark age. Idealism was shattered, and the Esperanto movement declined. It was not until after 1918 that the Esperanto movement in China, awakened by the May Fourth Movement, started again. At that time, the Esperanto movement focused on practical applications, the compilation and printing of Esperanto research books, the publication of magazines and publications, the establishment of tutoring classes and correspondence schools in various places, and the beginning of attention to Esperanto by the vocational circles (such as the postal and telecommunications circles), this period being the most prosperous. At the same time, debates on the structure and effectiveness of Esperanto writing and the relationship between Esperanto and the national language attracted the attention of the general public during this period. Therefore, this period can be called the (practical period) of the Esperanto movement.

The Great Revolution of 1926-7 came. The Esperanto movement was gradually ignored by people. However, after the political and social turmoil temporarily passed, the Esperanto movement made a comeback, but it changed its face and entered the (struggle period) from the (practical era). Originally, after 1926, China's national liberation movement had a close relationship with the international broad liberation movement. China was moving towards the road of struggle, and Esperanto, because it is a sharp tool to communicate the feelings of various nations, especially to promote the solidarity of the masses of various countries, can become a tool of struggle. Therefore, in this period, Esperanto is no longer just a pastime for the leisure class, and Esperantoism is no longer a paralyzing illusion of peace.

Therefore, it can be seen that Esperanto and the Esperanto movement are not super-historical categories. On the contrary, they are constantly developing and growing with the changes of the times. In the early days of the Esperanto movement, China was in the enlightenment period of cultural innovation, and the utopian doctrine of peace and fraternity represented the ideological characteristics of the time, so the so-called (internal ideal) became the keynote of the Esperanto movement at that time. However, this era has disappeared, and the Esperanto ideal representing this era cannot but disappear. Even if you want to point out the old brand and be infatuated with the bones, what's the use? The Esperanto movement in the second period was relatively practical, but it rose with the rise of the Chinese petty bourgeoisie after the May Fourth Movement. This era is now collapsing, so the pragmatic view of Esperanto still cannot be built. We only have to see that the early advocates of Esperanto not only no longer talk about Esperanto and peace and fraternity, but also become obstacles to all cultural innovations, which shows that the first period of the Esperanto movement is dead. Looking again at Mr. Yiguxuantong, who advocated Esperanto most vigorously in the May Fourth era, did not study Esperanto himself, practical Esperanto, so what kind of achievements the pragmatic Esperanto movement has achieved can be imagined.

The era that has passed has passed, and the era that has died has died, but Esperanto and the Esperanto movement have not died, and have been reborn. If the veteran Esperanto speakers are tired of Esperanto and leave the Esperanto movement, young people and the working masses begin to pay attention to Esperanto and support the Esperanto movement. Naturally, young people and the masses need Esperanto, not to paralyze themselves, construct their own fantasies, let alone for personal use, but to use Esperanto for social use. Only by recognizing the social significance of the Esperanto movement can we not misuse Esperanto. Only from here can we find the broad future of the Esperanto movement.

China, like many Eastern countries, will leap from the backward state of economic and cultural to the forefront of the times. A great struggle is unfolding. Therefore, the Esperanto movement in China has a very important task. The development of the Esperanto movement in the East in recent years is faster than in the West. In particular, Esperanto speakers in Japan have made greater efforts than any other country. This is by no means accidental. Easterners who are catching up with the times need Esperanto as a tool more urgently than Westerners.

Therefore, the future of the Esperanto movement in China is unlimited. At present, there are many difficulties in front of us. The development of this new stage of the Esperanto movement is only a glimmer of dawn. Only young people can take responsibility, overcome all difficulties, and make Esperanto embark on a broad new path.

Esperanto Movement in Shanghai

— Chu Deming

Shanghai is a so-called "cosmopolitan" international city and also the current cultural center of China. Therefore, the general public is more sensitive to international culture and international language issues than people in the hinterland. Furthermore, because the Esperanto movement has a longer history in Shanghai, the Esperanto movement in Shanghai is of great significance to the entire Chinese Esperanto movement.

It is said that in 1906, Mr. Liu Shipei established a training class in Shanghai, which may be the pioneer of the Esperanto movement in Shanghai. The following year, Mr. Lu Shikai also opened a class in Shanghai to teach. I don't know what happened to Mr. Liu now. The reporter has met Mr. Lu a few times, and it is said that he came into contact with Russians due to commercial relations. Mr. Lu learned Esperanto from a Russian. In 1909, the "Chinese Esperanto Association" was established in Shanghai, which was later reorganized into the "Republic of China Esperanto Association." It also opened correspondence courses, published magazines, and established branches in Changshu, Nanjing, and other places. This was more than twenty years ago, so the detailed situation is not very clear.

Around 1927, the Jiangwan Labor University included Esperanto in its curriculum. The professor was the Japanese Yamaga Taiji, who used the direct teaching method (i.e., without Chinese translation). Later, Yamaga left Shanghai and returned to Japan, and Mr. Zhu Zhenjiang, the school doctor, took over. The Esperanto movement in Shanghai was quite powerful for a time.

In schools, Fudan University and Lida Academy and other schools have successively organized Esperanto societies. However, during the "January 28th Incident," not only Jiangwan and Zhabei were baptized by the artillery fire of the "Imperial Army," but the Esperanto movement in Shanghai was also fatally hit. At that time, the "Shanghai Esperanto Society," located in Zhabei, suffered great losses, and its affairs came to a standstill. Although the movement was interrupted on the surface, some young Esperantists in Shanghai did not forget their mission under the threat of artillery fire! It is said that at that time, many comrades organized the "International Propaganda Committee" to expose the armed attacks of Japanese imperialism to the world in Esperanto, and won the sympathetic support of various countries.

Soon after the January 28th Incident, the "Chinese Esperanto Correspondence School" was also established. At that time, it was the only place in Shanghai that spread Esperanto. In December 1932, the "Chinese Esperanto Correspondence School" launched the Esperanto Exhibition, which was even more successful. In January 1933, the "Shanghai Esperantists Association" was established, and the Esperanto movement in Shanghai began to develop vigorously again.

Now let's describe the existing Esperanto organizations in Shanghai:

The Shanghai International Esperanto Association was established in the spring of this year. Its members include Chinese, Japanese, British, Austrian, and other nationalities, so it is named the "Shanghai International Esperanto Association." Because it was established not long ago, there are only dozens of members. A certain radio station in this city once broadcast Esperanto lessons by the association, and there were many learners for a while. The association had planned to open a training class, but it has not been realized due to various difficulties. The association welcomes people from all countries to join. The membership fee is five cents per month, and the mailing address is Shanghai P.O. Box 1871.

The Shanghai Esperanto Society is one of the most powerful Esperanto organizations in China and was established very early. In the past, it was in (students
